ResultNow I have comprehensive knowledge of all the APIs. Let me compile the full implementation plan. --- # Paywalled Blog Demo -- Implementation Plan ## 1. Project Overview and Architecture The project is a Next.js App Router application with TypeScript and Tailwind CSS. It integrates three external services -- Sanity CMS (content), Stripe (payments), and ThirdWeb (wallet-based auth) -- and provides a fully functional visual demo at `/demo` that works even when environment variables are absent. **Root directory:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b` --- ## 2. Complete File Tree ``` / ├── .env.local.example # Template for all env vars ├── .gitignore ├── next.config.ts ├── package.json ├── postcss.config.mjs ├── tailwind.config.ts ├── tsconfig.json │ ├── public/ │ └── fonts/ │ ├── futura-medium.woff2 # Home page: blog post listing │ │ │ ├── (blog)/ # Route group for blog content │ │ └── posts/ │ │ └── [slug]/ │ │ └── page.tsx # Individual blog post page with paywall │ │ │ ├── demo/ │ │ └── page.tsx # Styled button component │ │ │ └── lib/ │ ├── stripe.ts # loadStripe singleton + env check │ ├── thirdweb.ts # createThirdwebClient + env check │ ├── constants.ts # Demo content, brand colors │ └── utils.ts # cn() helper, etc. │ └── types/ └── index.ts # Shared TypeScript types (Post, Author) ``` --- ## 3. Step-by-Step Implementation ### Phase 1: Project Scaffolding **Step 1.1 -- Initialize Next.js project** Run inside the project directory: ```bash npx create-next-app@latest . --typescript --tailwind --eslint --app --src-dir --import-alias "@/*" ``` This generates the standard Next.js skeleton with App Router, TypeScript, Tailwind CSS v4, and the `src/` directory layout. The `--import-alias "@/*"` sets up path aliases in `tsconfig.json`. **Step 1.2 -- Install all dependencies** Production dependencies: ```bash npm install next-sanity @sanity/image-url sanity @sanity/vision \ @stripe/stripe-js @stripe/react-stripe-js stripe \ thirdweb \ @portabletext/react ``` Dev dependencies (most come from create-next-app, but add): ```bash npm install -D @types/node ``` Package rationale: - `next-sanity` -- Sanity client for Next.js, `createClient`, `defineQuery`, `NextStudio` - `sanity` + `@sanity/vision` -- Sanity Studio itself (embedded at `/studio`) and the GROQ query testing plugin - `@sanity/image-url` -- Generates image URLs from Sanity image assets - `@stripe/stripe-js` -- Client-side Stripe.js loader (`loadStripe`) - `@stripe/react-stripe-js` -- React components: `Elements`, `PaymentElement`, `ExpressCheckoutElement` - `stripe` -- Server-side Stripe SDK (used in the API route to create PaymentIntents) - `thirdweb` -- v5 SDK; imports from `thirdweb/react`, `thirdweb/wallets`, `thirdweb` (replaces the old `@thirdweb-dev/react` and `@thirdweb-dev/sdk`) - `@portabletext/react` -- Renders Sanity Portable Text (rich text body content) **Step 1.3 -- Create `.env.local.example`** ``` # Sanity NEXT_PUBLIC_SANITY_PROJECT_ID= NEXT_PUBLIC_SANITY_DATASET=production SANITY_API_READ_TOKEN= # Stripe NEXT_PUBLIC_STRIPE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY= STRIPE_SECRET_KEY= # ThirdWeb NEXT_PUBLIC_THIRDWEB_CLIENT_ID= ``` **Step 1.4 -- Configure fonts and global styles in `src/app/globals.css`** Use `@font-face` to load Futura (self-hosted woff2 files in `public/fonts/`) with a fallback to `"Century Gothic", "Trebuchet MS", Arial, sans-serif`. Define Helvetica as the body font stack: `"Helvetica Neue", Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif`. Set up Tailwind CSS directives and custom CSS variables for brand colors. In `tailwind.config.ts`, extend `fontFamily`: ```ts fontFamily: { title: ['"Futura"', '"Century Gothic"', 'sans-serif'], body: ['"Helvetica Neue"', 'Helvetica', 'Arial', 'sans-serif'], } ``` --- ### Phase 2: Sanity CMS Configuration **Step 2.1 -- Environment helper: `sanity/env.ts`** Export `projectId`, `dataset`, and `apiVersion` with fallbacks: ```ts export const projectId = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SANITY_PROJECT_ID || 'placeholder'; export const dataset = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SANITY_DATASET || 'production'; export const apiVersion = '2024-12-01'; ``` The `'placeholder'` string is intentional -- the Sanity client will fail gracefully when queries are attempted, and the demo page does not depend on live Sanity data. **Step 2.2 -- Sanity client: `sanity/lib/client.ts`** ```ts import { createClient } from 'next-sanity'; import { projectId, dataset, apiVersion } from '../env'; export const client = createClient({ projectId, dataset, apiVersion, useCdn: true, }); ``` **Step 2.3 -- Image URL helper: `sanity/lib/image.ts`** ```ts import imageUrlBuilder from '@sanity/image-url'; import { client } from './client'; const builder = imageUrlBuilder(client); export function urlFor(source: any) { return builder.image(source); } ``` **Step 2.4 -- Schemas: `sanity/schemas/author.ts`** ```ts import { defineType, defineField } from 'sanity'; export const authorType = defineType({ name: 'author', title: 'Author', type: 'document', fields: [ defineField({ name: 'name', type: 'string', validation: (r) => r.required() }), defineField({ name: 'slug', type: 'slug', options: { source: 'name' }, validation: (r) => r.required() }), defineField({ name: 'avatar', type: 'image', options: { hotspot: true } }), defineField({ name: 'bio', type: 'text' }), ], }); ``` **Step 2.5 -- Schemas: `sanity/schemas/post.ts`** ```ts import { defineType, defineField } from 'sanity'; export const postType = defineType({ name: 'post', title: 'Post', type: 'document', fields: [ defineField({ name: 'title', type: 'string', validation: (r) => r.required() }), defineField({ name: 'slug', type: 'slug', options: { source: 'title' }, validation: (r) => r.required() }), defineField({ name: 'excerpt', type: 'text', rows: 3 }), defineField({ name: 'featuredImage', type: 'image', options: { hotspot: true } }), defineField({ name: 'author', type: 'reference', to: [{ type: 'author' }] }), defineField({ name: 'publishedAt', type: 'datetime' }), defineField({ name: 'isPremium', title: 'Premium Content', type: 'boolean', description: 'Toggle to enable paywall for this post', initialValue: false, }), defineField({ name: 'body', type: 'array', of: [{ type: 'block' }, { type: 'image', options: { hotspot: true } }], }), ], preview: { select: { title: 'title', subtitle: 'author.name', media: 'featuredImage' }, }, }); ``` The `isPremium` boolean is the paywall toggle. When true, the frontend renders the `PaywallOverlay` on top of the article. **Step 2.6 -- Schema index: `sanity/schemas/index.ts`** ```ts import { postType } from './post'; import { authorType } from './author'; export const schemaTypes = [postType, authorType]; ``` **Step 2.7 -- Sanity Studio config: `sanity.config.ts` (project root)** ```ts import { defineConfig } from 'sanity'; import { structureTool } from 'sanity/structure'; import { visionTool } from '@sanity/vision'; import { schemaTypes } from './sanity/schemas'; import { projectId, dataset, apiVersion } from './sanity/env'; export default defineConfig({ name: 'default', title: 'Paywalled Blog', projectId, dataset, apiVersion, basePath: '/studio', plugins: [structureTool(), visionTool()], schema: { types: schemaTypes }, }); ``` **Step 2.8 -- Embedded Studio route: `src/app/studio/[[...tool]]/page.tsx`** ```tsx 'use client'; import { NextStudio } from 'next-sanity/studio'; import config from '../../../../sanity.config'; export default function StudioPage() { return <NextStudio config={config} />; } ``` This is a catch-all route so all Sanity Studio sub-routes (desk, vision, etc.) work. Mark it `'use client'` because the Studio is a client-side app. **Step 2.9 -- GROQ queries: `sanity/lib/queries.ts`** ```ts import { defineQuery } from 'next-sanity'; export const POSTS_QUERY = defineQuery( `*[_type == "post" && defined(slug.current)] | order(publishedAt desc)[0...12]{ _id, title, slug, excerpt, featuredImage, publishedAt, isPremium, author->{ name, slug, avatar } }` ); export const POST_BY_SLUG_QUERY = defineQuery( `*[_type == "post" && slug.current == $slug][0]{ _id, title, slug, excerpt, featuredImage, publishedAt, isPremium, body, author->{ name, slug, avatar, bio } }` ); ``` --- ### Phase 3: Stripe Integration **Step 3.1 -- Stripe client singleton: `src/app/lib/stripe.ts`** ```ts import { loadStripe, Stripe } from '@stripe/stripe-js'; let stripePromise: Promise<Stripe | null> | null = null; export const getStripe = () => { const key = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_STRIPE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY; if (!key) return null; // graceful fallback if (!stripePromise) { stripePromise = loadStripe(key); } return stripePromise; }; export const isStripeConfigured = (): boolean => !!process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_STRIPE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY; ``` **Step 3.2 -- Server API route: `src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts`** ```ts import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'; import Stripe from 'stripe'; export async function POST(request: Request) { const secretKey = process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY; if (!secretKey) { return NextResponse.json( { error: 'Stripe is not configured' }, { status: 503 } ); } const stripe = new Stripe(secretKey, { apiVersion: '2024-12-18.acacia' }); try { const { amount = 999 } = await request.json(); const paymentIntent = await stripe.paymentIntents.create({ amount, currency: 'usd', automatic_payment_methods: { enabled: true }, }); return NextResponse.json({ clientSecret: paymentIntent.client_secret }); } catch (err: any) { return NextResponse.json({ error: err.message }, { status: 500 }); } } ``` The `automatic_payment_methods: { enabled: true }` is critical -- this lets Stripe dynamically show Apple Pay, Google Pay, Link, and card payments based on the customer's device capabilities. **Step 3.3 -- StripeProvider: `src/app/components/providers/StripeProvider.tsx`** A client component that wraps children in `<Elements>`. It fetches a `clientSecret` from the API route on mount. If Stripe is not configured, it renders children without the provider (fallback to mock UI). ```tsx 'use client'; import { useState, useEffect, ReactNode } from 'react'; import { Elements } from '@stripe/react-stripe-js'; import { getStripe, isStripeConfigured } from '@/app/lib/stripe'; import type { Appearance } from '@stripe/stripe-js'; const appearance: Appearance = { theme: 'flat', variables: { fontFamily: '"Helvetica Neue", Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif', colorPrimary: '#0a2540', }, }; export function StripeProvider({ children }: { children: ReactNode }) { const [clientSecret, setClientSecret] = useState<string | null>(null); const stripePromise = getStripe(); useEffect(() => { if (!isStripeConfigured()) return; fetch('/api/stripe/create-payment-intent', { method: 'POST', headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' }, body: JSON.stringify({ amount: 999 }), }) .then((res) => res.json()) .then((data) => setClientSecret(data.clientSecret)) .catch(console.error); }, []); if (!stripePromise || !clientSecret) { return <>{children}</>; // renders mock UI } return ( <Elements stripe={stripePromise} options={{ clientSecret, appearance }}> {children} </Elements> ); } ``` **Step 3.4 -- StripeCheckout component: `src/app/components/paywall/StripeCheckout.tsx`** A client component that renders both `<PaymentElement>` (card form) and `<ExpressCheckoutElement>` (Apple Pay / Google Pay buttons) inside the paywall overlay. It uses `useStripe()` and `useElements()` hooks, and calls `stripe.confirmPayment()` on form submit. **Step 3.5 -- MockStripeCheckout: `src/app/components/paywall/MockStripeCheckout.tsx`** A purely visual component that renders a static card-form-looking UI and fake Apple Pay / Google Pay buttons. This is displayed when `isStripeConfigured()` returns false, ensuring the demo page always looks complete. Use Tailwind to style it identically to a real Stripe form. The Apple Pay button uses the standard black rounded-rect style; the Google Pay button uses the standard white rounded-rect with the "G" logo. --- ### Phase 4: ThirdWeb Integration **Step 4.1 -- ThirdWeb client: `src/app/lib/thirdweb.ts`** ```ts import { createThirdwebClient } from 'thirdweb'; const clientId = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_THIRDWEB_CLIENT_ID; export const thirdwebClient = clientId ? createThirdwebClient({ clientId }) : null; export const isThirdWebConfigured = (): boolean => !!clientId; ``` **Step 4.2 -- ThirdWebProvider: `src/app/components/providers/ThirdWebProvider.tsx`** ```tsx 'use client'; import { ThirdwebProvider } from 'thirdweb/react'; import { ReactNode } from 'react'; import { isThirdWebConfigured } from '@/app/lib/thirdweb'; export function ThirdWebProviderWrapper({ children }: { children: ReactNode }) { if (!isThirdWebConfigured()) return <>{children}</>; return <ThirdwebProvider>{children}</ThirdwebProvider>; } ``` **Step 4.3 -- ThirdWebAuth component: `src/app/components/auth/ThirdWebAuth.tsx`** When configured, renders the real ThirdWeb `ConnectButton` with in-app wallet supporting social login: ```tsx 'use client'; import { ConnectButton } from 'thirdweb/react'; import { inAppWallet } from 'thirdweb/wallets'; import { thirdwebClient, isThirdWebConfigured } from '@/app/lib/thirdweb'; import { MockThirdWebAuth } from './MockThirdWebAuth'; const wallets = [ inAppWallet({ auth: { options: ['google', 'apple', 'facebook', 'email'] }, }), ]; export function ThirdWebAuth() { if (!isThirdWebConfigured() || !thirdwebClient) { return <MockThirdWebAuth />; } return ( <ConnectButton client={thirdwebClient} wallets={wallets} connectButton={{ label: 'Sign in with Social' }} /> ); } ``` **Step 4.4 -- MockThirdWebAuth: `src/app/components/auth/MockThirdWebAuth.tsx`** A styled button that visually mimics the ConnectButton. On click, it shows a toast or small modal saying "ThirdWeb not configured -- set NEXT_PUBLIC_THIRDWEB_CLIENT_ID". Uses the same font styling and dimensions as the real component. --- ### Phase 5: Paywall Overlay This is the centerpiece UI -- a full-viewport overlay that sits on top of blurred article content, replicating the NYT/Washington Post paywall experience. **Step 5.1 -- PaywallOverlay: `src/app/components/paywall/PaywallOverlay.tsx`** Architecture: - The article content is rendered normally behind the overlay. - A CSS gradient fade (white-to-transparent going upward) covers the bottom 60% of the article. - On top of that, a fixed/absolute-positioned overlay with `backdrop-filter: blur(6px)` and a semi-transparent background. - Inside the overlay: a centered card containing the payment/auth UI. ```tsx 'use client'; import { useState } from 'react'; import { StripeCheckout } from './StripeCheckout'; import { MockStripeCheckout } from './MockStripeCheckout'; import { ThirdWebAuth } from '../auth/ThirdWebAuth'; import { isStripeConfigured } from '@/app/lib/stripe'; export function PaywallOverlay() { const [dismissed, setDismissed] = useState(false); if (dismissed) return null; return ( <div className="fixed inset-0 z-50 flex items-end justify-center"> {/* Background blur + fade */} <div className="absolute inset-0 bg-gradient-to-t from-white via-white/95 to-transparent" /> <div className="absolute inset-0 backdrop-blur-sm" /> {/* Paywall card */} <div className="relative z-10 w-full max-w-lg mx-auto mb-12 bg-white rounded-2xl shadow-2xl p-8 border border-gray-200"> <h2 className="font-title text-2xl font-bold text-center mb-2"> Subscribe to continue reading </h2> <p className="font-body text-gray-600 text-center mb-6"> Get unlimited access to premium articles for $9.99/month </p> {/* ThirdWeb social sign-in */} <div className="mb-6"> <p className="text-sm text-gray-500 text-center mb-3"> Already a member? Sign in </p> <div className="flex justify-center"> <ThirdWebAuth /> </div> </div> <div className="border-t border-gray-200 my-6" /> {/* Stripe payment */} {isStripeConfigured() ? <StripeCheckout /> : <MockStripeCheckout />} </div> </div> ); } ``` Key styling decisions: - `font-title` class uses Futura (configured in Tailwind). - `font-body` class uses Helvetica. - The gradient goes from fully opaque white at the bottom to transparent at the top, so the article text fades out naturally. - The card is `max-w-lg`, centered, with rounded corners and shadow -- matching modern paywall aesthetics. --- ### Phase 6: Blog Components **Step 6.1 -- BlogPost: `src/app/components/blog/BlogPost.tsx`** Renders a full blog post: title (Futura), author badge, published date, featured image, and body content (via `@portabletext/react`). Accepts a `isPremium` prop; when true, the component co-renders the `PaywallOverlay`. Layout pattern: ```tsx <article className="relative"> <header> <h1 className="font-title text-4xl font-bold">{title}</h1> <AuthorBadge author={author} date={publishedAt} /> {featuredImage && <img ... />} </header> <div className={isPremium ? 'max-h-[600px] overflow-hidden' : ''}> <PortableText value={body} /> </div> {isPremium && <PaywallOverlay />} </article> ``` The `max-h-[600px] overflow-hidden` truncates the article body so only the first portion is visible, reinforcing the paywall effect. **Step 6.2 -- BlogPostCard: `src/app/components/blog/BlogPostCard.tsx`** A card component for the listing page. Shows featured image, title, excerpt, author, and a "Premium" badge when `isPremium` is true. **Step 6.3 -- AuthorBadge: `src/app/components/blog/AuthorBadge.tsx`** Small component: author avatar (circular), name, and formatted date. --- ### Phase 7: The Demo Page **Step 7.1 -- Constants file: `src/app/lib/constants.ts`** Contains hardcoded demo content so the `/demo` page works without any external services: ```ts export const DEMO_POST = { title: 'The Future of Decentralized Media', author: { name: 'Jane Nakamoto', avatar: null }, publishedAt: '2025-01-15T10:00:00Z', isPremium: true, excerpt: 'How blockchain technology is reshaping content monetization...', body: [ // 6-8 paragraphs of placeholder text (NOT lorem ipsum -- actual // readable placeholder about decentralized media, Web3, creator // economies, etc.) ], }; ``` **Step 7.2 -- Demo page: `src/app/demo/page.tsx`** This is a self-contained page that renders the full paywall experience using hardcoded data. It does NOT depend on Sanity, Stripe, or ThirdWeb being configured. It imports mock components as fallbacks. ```tsx import { DEMO_POST } from '@/app/lib/constants'; import { BlogPost } from '@/app/components/blog/BlogPost'; import { ThirdWebProviderWrapper } from '@/app/components/providers/ThirdWebProvider'; import { StripeProvider } from '@/app/components/providers/StripeProvider'; export const metadata = { title: 'Paywall Demo', description: 'Interactive demo of the paywalled blog experience', }; export default function DemoPage() { return ( <ThirdWebProviderWrapper> <StripeProvider> <main className="min-h-screen bg-white"> <div className="max-w-3xl mx-auto px-4 py-12"> <BlogPost title={DEMO_POST.title} author={DEMO_POST.author} publishedAt={DEMO_POST.publishedAt} isPremium={DEMO_POST.isPremium} body={DEMO_POST.body} excerpt={DEMO_POST.excerpt} featuredImage={null} /> </div> </main> </StripeProvider> </ThirdWebProviderWrapper> ); } ``` The provider wrappers detect missing env vars and pass through without wrapping, so the mock UI components render in their place. The page is always visually complete. --- ### Phase 8: Dynamic Blog Pages (Sanity-powered) **Step 8.1 -- Home page: `src/app/page.tsx`** An async Server Component that fetches posts from Sanity using `POSTS_QUERY`. Wraps the fetch in a try/catch; on failure (Sanity not configured), falls back to showing the demo post card with a link to `/demo`. **Step 8.2 -- Post detail page: `src/app/(blog)/posts/[slug]/page.tsx`** An async Server Component that fetches a single post by slug using `POST_BY_SLUG_QUERY`. If the post has `isPremium: true`, it wraps the page in the providers and renders `BlogPost` with the `PaywallOverlay`. If Sanity fetch fails, redirects to `/demo`. --- ### Phase 9: Root Layout and Providers **Step 9.1 -- Root layout: `src/app/layout.tsx`** ```tsx import type { Metadata } from 'next'; import './globals.css'; export const metadata: Metadata = { title: 'Paywalled Blog', description: 'A demo paywalled blog with Sanity CMS, Stripe, and ThirdWeb', }; export default function RootLayout({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) { return ( <html lang="en"> <body className="font-body antialiased text-gray-900"> <header className="border-b border-gray-200 py-4 px-6"> <nav className="max-w-5xl mx-auto flex items-center justify-between"> <a href="/" className="font-title text-xl font-bold"> The Paywall Times </a> <div className="flex items-center gap-4"> <a href="/demo" className="text-sm text-gray-600 hover:text-black"> Demo </a> <a href="/studio" className="text-sm text-gray-600 hover:text-black"> Studio </a> </div> </nav> </header> {children} </body> </html> ); } ``` Providers (ThirdWeb, Stripe) are NOT in the root layout. They are only mounted on pages that need them (demo, individual premium posts) to avoid unnecessary SDK loading. --- ### Phase 10: TypeScript Types **Step 10.1 -- `types/index.ts`** ```ts export interface Author { name: string; slug?: { current: string }; avatar?: any; // Sanity image reference bio?: string; } export interface Post { _id?: string; title: string; slug?: { current: string }; excerpt?: string; featuredImage?: any; author?: Author; publishedAt?: string; isPremium: boolean; body?: any[]; // Portable Text blocks } ``` --- ## 4. Key Design Decisions Explained **Why `thirdweb` (v5) instead of `@thirdweb-dev/react` (v4)?** The v4 packages are deprecated as of June 2025. The v5 SDK uses a single `thirdweb` package with sub-path imports (`thirdweb/react`, `thirdweb/wallets`), is tree-shakeable, and supports the same `ConnectButton` and `inAppWallet` APIs. **Why `PaymentElement` + `ExpressCheckoutElement` instead of Stripe Checkout (redirect)?** The requirement specifies a popup overlay sitting on top of blurred content, exactly like NYT/WashPost. Stripe Checkout redirects to a hosted page, which breaks this UX. `PaymentElement` renders inline, and `ExpressCheckoutElement` provides the Apple Pay / Google Pay buttons (Stripe explicitly states wallet payments should use `ExpressCheckoutElement` to avoid duplication with `PaymentElement`). **Why are providers scoped to specific pages, not the root layout?** Both the Stripe Elements SDK and the ThirdWeb SDK load significant JavaScript. Wrapping them at the root layout would penalize every page (home listing, studio, etc.) with unnecessary bundle weight. Instead, only the `/demo` page and individual premium post pages mount the providers. **Why separate Mock components instead of conditional rendering inside the real components?** Clean separation of concerns. The mock components have zero dependency on external SDKs -- they are pure HTML/CSS. This means: (a) the demo page renders instantly without any SDK initialization, (b) there is no risk of runtime errors from uninitialized Stripe/ThirdWeb contexts, and (c) mock and real components can be styled independently. **Why is the Sanity Studio embedded at `/studio` instead of deployed separately?** The requirement says "embedded at /studio or configured separately." Embedding keeps the demo self-contained: a single `npm run dev` command gives you the blog, the demo page, and the content management studio. The catch-all route `[[...tool]]` handles all Studio sub-routes. Route groups `(blog)` ensure the Studio layout (which is full-viewport, no header) does not conflict with the blog layout. **Graceful degradation strategy:** Every external service integration follows the same pattern: (1) check for env var at module level, (2) export an `isXConfigured()` function, (3) provider wrappers pass through when unconfigured, (4) UI components swap to mock variants. The demo page at `/demo` always works because it uses hardcoded content and falls back to mock payment/auth UI. --- ## 5. Implementation Sequencing The recommended order for building this: 1. **Scaffold** (Phase 1) -- 5 minutes. Get the Next.js project running with Tailwind. 2. **Types** (Phase 10) -- Define types first so everything downstream is typed. 3. **Constants** (Phase 7, Step 7.1) -- Hardcode demo content early; it unblocks UI work. 4. **UI components** (Phase 6 + Phase 5 mocks) -- Build `BlogPost`, `BlogPostCard`, `AuthorBadge`, `MockStripeCheckout`, `MockThirdWebAuth`, `PaywallOverlay`. At this point, the demo page can render with pure mock UI. 5. **Demo page** (Phase 7, Step 7.2) -- Wire up the demo page. Verify the visual paywall experience. 6. **Stripe integration** (Phase 3) -- Add the real Stripe provider, API route, and `StripeCheckout` component. Test with test keys. 7. **ThirdWeb integration** (Phase 4) -- Add the real ThirdWeb provider and `ThirdWebAuth`. Test with a ThirdWeb client ID. 8. **Sanity schemas and client** (Phase 2) -- Set up schemas, client, queries. 9. **Sanity Studio** (Phase 2, Step 2.8) -- Embed Studio at `/studio`. 10. **Dynamic blog pages** (Phase 8) -- Wire up home page and `[slug]` page to Sanity. 11. **Root layout and polish** (Phase 9) -- Final layout, navigation, responsive tweaks. --- ## 6. Potential Challenges and Mitigations | Challenge | Mitigation | |---|---| | Futura is a commercial font; cannot be freely distributed | Ship with fallback stack (`Century Gothic`, `Trebuchet MS`). Include a README note about licensing. If Futura is available on the system, CSS will use it via `font-family`. | | Apple Pay requires HTTPS and domain verification | Document this in README. For local dev, Apple Pay simply does not appear (Stripe handles this gracefully). The mock UI always shows the Apple Pay button for visual completeness. | | `next-sanity`'s `NextStudio` may conflict with the blog layout | Use a route group `(blog)` for content pages and keep `/studio` outside it. The Studio page has no shared layout with blog pages. | | ThirdWeb SDK requires a valid client ID for any wallet connection | The `MockThirdWebAuth` component provides a visual substitute. The real `ConnectButton` only mounts when `NEXT_PUBLIC_THIRDWEB_CLIENT_ID` is present. | | Stripe `PaymentIntent` creation fails without `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` | The API route returns 503. The `StripeProvider` detects missing config and renders children without `<Elements>`, which triggers the mock UI. | --- ### Critical Files for Implementation - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/paywall/PaywallOverlay.tsx` - Centerpiece of the entire project; orchestrates the blur overlay, Stripe checkout, and ThirdWeb auth into the NYT-style paywall experience - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/demo/page.tsx` - The self-contained demo page that must work without any env vars; wires together all providers and components with hardcoded content - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/sanity/schemas/post.ts` - Defines the post schema including the critical `isPremium` boolean toggle that drives paywall behavior - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/providers/StripeProvider.tsx` - Manages the Elements context with graceful fallback; controls whether real or mock Stripe UI renders - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts` - Server-side route that creates PaymentIntents with `automatic_payment_methods` enabled for Apple Pay/Google Pay support agentId: aff0e0879694de7e7 (use SendMessage with to: 'aff0e0879694de7e7' to continue this agent) <usage>total_tokens: 39966 tool_uses: 21 duration_ms: 472752</usage>

`types/index.ts`: `Post`, `Author` interfaces - `src/app/lib/constants.ts`: Hardcoded demo post (6-8 paragraphs about decentralized media) ### Step 4: Sanity CMS schemas - `author.ts`: name, slug, avatar, bio - `post.ts`: title, slug, excerpt, featuredImage, author ref, publishedAt, **isPremium** (boolean toggle), body (Portable Text) - Sanity client, queries, image helper, env config - Embedded Studio at `/studio` via `NextStudio` ### Step 5: Mock UI components (no SDK dependency) - **MockStripeCheckout**: Static card form + Apple Pay/Google Pay buttons styled to match Stripe - **MockThirdWebAuth**: Social sign-in button matching ThirdWeb ConnectButton style ### Step 6: PaywallOverlay component (centerpiece) - Gradient fade from white (bottom) to transparent (top) over article content - Backdrop blur behind the overlay card - Centered card with: - "Subscribe to continue reading" (Futura) - Price copy (Helvetica) - ThirdWeb sign-in ("Already a member?") - Divider - Stripe checkout (Apple Pay/Google Pay + card form) ### Step 7: Blog components - `BlogPost`: Renders article with `max-h` + overflow hidden when premium, mounts PaywallOverlay - `AuthorBadge`: Avatar + name + date ### Step 8: Stripe integration - `lib/stripe.ts`: `loadStripe` singleton with env check - `StripeProvider`: Fetches `clientSecret` from API route, wraps in `<Elements>` with branded appearance - `StripeCheckout`: `ExpressCheckoutElement` (Apple/Google Pay) + `PaymentElement` (card) - API route: Creates PaymentIntent with `automatic_payment_methods: { enabled: true }` ### Step 9: ThirdWeb integration - `lib/thirdweb.ts`: `createThirdwebClient` with env check - `ThirdWebProvider`: Wraps in `<ThirdwebProvider>` or passes through - `ThirdWebAuth`: `ConnectButton` with `inAppWallet` supporting google, apple, facebook, email ### Step 10: Demo page + root layout - `/demo`: Self-contained page using hardcoded content, mock components as fallback - Root layout: Nav bar with "The Paywall Times" branding, links to Demo + Studio - Home page: Lists posts from Sanity (falls back to demo card) ## Key Design Decisions - **thirdweb v5** (single `thirdweb` package) — v4 `@thirdweb-dev/*` is deprecated - **PaymentElement + ExpressCheckoutElement** (not Stripe Checkout redirect) — stays inline for the popup overlay UX - **Separate mock components** — zero SDK dependency, instant render, no runtime errors - **Futura fallback stack** — Futura is commercial; falls back to Century Gothic → Trebuchet MS. Note: user can drop in .woff2 files later ## Verification 1. `npm run dev` → home page loads with nav bar 2. `/demo` → full article with paywall overlay, mock Apple Pay/Google Pay buttons, mock sign-in 3. `/studio` → Sanity Studio loads (will show config error without project ID, which is expected) 4. Paying does **nothing**. There's no state change, no content unlock, no subscription record. ### If you add env vars With real keys in `.env.local`, the mock components get replaced: 1. **Stripe flow:** `StripeProvider` calls `/api/stripe/create-payment-intent` → creates a one-time $9.99 PaymentIntent → renders real `PaymentElement` + `ExpressCheckoutElement`. Want me to wire that up?
User (Turn 6)15:44:23
How does the paywall know where to mint a membership after payment if the user isn't signed in with ThirdWeb/
Assistant15:44:43
It doesn't — that's an unresolved gap in the current implementation. There's no connection between Stripe payment and ThirdWeb wallet at all right now. ## The problem To mint a membership NFT, you need a **wallet address** to mint to. If the user just pays with Stripe and never signs in with ThirdWeb, there's no wallet to target. ## How it should work The correct flow requires **sign-in before payment**: 1. **User signs in via ThirdWeb** — the `inAppWallet` with email/Google/Apple automatically creates a wallet for them behind the scenes (they never see seed phrases or MetaMask) 2. **Wallet address is captured** — stored in state/context 3. **User pays via Stripe** — the PaymentIntent metadata includes the wallet address 4. **Stripe webhook confirms payment** — backend calls a smart contract to mint the membership NFT to that wallet 5. **Paywall checks access** — reads the connected wallet, checks if it holds the membership token, removes the overlay if it does ## What's wrong with the current UI The overlay shows "Already a member? Sign in" as a secondary option below the Stripe form. That's backwards. Sign-in should be **step one**, with Stripe only appearing after a wallet is connected. Otherwise there's nowhere to mint. ## What's missing to close this loop - A shared auth context that holds the connected wallet address - Enforcing sign-in before showing the payment form - Passing the wallet address to the Stripe PaymentIntent metadata - A Stripe webhook route that triggers the NFT mint - A smart contract for the membership token - A paywall check that reads token ownership from the wallet Want me to restructure the flow so sign-in comes first and wire the pieces together?

ResultI now have a thorough understanding of every file in the codebase. Let me present the complete implementation plan. --- ## Implementation Plan: Auth-First Paywall with NFT Membership Mint ### Architecture Overview The current codebase has a flat, prop-drilling architecture: the demo page renders `BlogPost`, which renders `PaywallOverlay`, which shows auth and Stripe side-by-side with no state coordination. The restructure introduces a shared React Context (`MembershipContext`) that orchestrates a two-step flow: authenticate first (capturing a wallet address), then pay (passing wallet address to Stripe metadata). On payment success, the context unlocks content and the overlay disappears. There are **1 new file** to create, **7 existing files** to modify, and **0 files to delete**. --- ### Step 1: Create MembershipContext **New file:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/providers/MembershipContext.tsx` This is the central coordination point for the entire flow. It must be a `"use client"` component. **Context shape:** ```typescript interface MembershipContextValue { // Auth state walletAddress: string | null; setWalletAddress: (address: string | null) => void; isAuthenticated: boolean; // Payment state paymentStatus: "idle" | "processing" | "succeeded" | "failed"; setPaymentStatus: (status: "idle" | "processing" | "succeeded" | "failed") => void; // Derived unlock state isUnlocked: boolean; } ``` **Implementation details:** - Use `createContext` with a `null` default, and a `useMembership()` hook that throws if used outside the provider (standard guarded-context pattern). - `isAuthenticated` is derived: `!!walletAddress`. - `isUnlocked` is derived: `paymentStatus === "succeeded"`. - State is held via two `useState` calls: `walletAddress` (string | null) and `paymentStatus` (enum string). - The provider component `MembershipProvider` wraps its `children` and exposes all values through `MembershipContextValue`. - Export the provider component and the `useMembership` hook. **Why a context and not prop drilling:** The wallet address needs to flow from `ThirdWebAuth` (or `MockThirdWebAuth`) down to `StripeProvider` (which calls the API with it), and the payment status needs to flow from `StripeCheckout` (or `MockStripeCheckout`) up to `BlogPost` (to remove the clip). Context avoids threading these through `PaywallOverlay`'s props, which would need to change BlogPost's interface too. --- ### Step 2: Update MockThirdWebAuth **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/auth/MockThirdWebAuth.tsx` **Current behavior:** Static button that shows an alert saying ThirdWeb is not configured. **Changes:** - Add `"use client"` directive (already present). - Import `useMembership` from the new context. - On click, instead of calling `alert()`, call `setWalletAddress("0xDEMO...1234")` -- a fake wallet address that simulates successful sign-in. - After setting wallet address, the button should visually change. Use `isAuthenticated` from context to conditionally render either the "Sign in to access" button or a signed-in state showing a truncated wallet address (e.g., `0xDEMO...1234`) with a green checkmark icon. - Add a "Sign out" option (small text link below the signed-in state) that calls `setWalletAddress(null)` to reset. **What stays the same:** The button styling, SVG icon, overall component structure. --- ### Step 3: Update ThirdWebAuth (Real SDK) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/auth/ThirdWebAuth.tsx` **Current behavior:** Renders ThirdWeb's `ConnectButton` with `inAppWallet`. Falls back to `MockThirdWebAuth` if no client ID. No state communication when user connects. **Changes:** - Import `useActiveAccount` from `thirdweb/react` and `useMembership` from context. - Add a `useEffect` that watches `useActiveAccount()`. When account becomes available (truthy), call `setWalletAddress(account.address)`. When account becomes `undefined` (user disconnects), call `setWalletAddress(null)`. - The fallback to `MockThirdWebAuth` stays as-is (the mock now also writes to context). - The `ConnectButton` rendering stays as-is -- ThirdWeb handles its own UI for the wallet connection flow. **Specific pattern:** ```typescript const account = useActiveAccount(); const { setWalletAddress } = useMembership(); useEffect(() => { setWalletAddress(account?.address ?? null); }, [account, setWalletAddress]); ``` **What stays the same:** The `ConnectButton` config, `inAppWallet` setup, fallback logic structure. --- ### Step 4: Update PaywallOverlay (Two-Step Flow) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/paywall/PaywallOverlay.tsx` **Current behavior:** Shows auth button and Stripe checkout simultaneously, separated by an "or" divider. No concept of steps. **Changes:** This is the most significant UI restructure. The overlay becomes a two-step flow: - Import `useMembership` from context. - Read `isAuthenticated` and `walletAddress` from context. - **Remove** the `stripeCheckout` and `authButton` props. The overlay will instead directly render the appropriate child components, and the step logic is driven by context state. However, to preserve the mock/real flexibility, **keep the props** but rename for clarity and change usage: - Keep `authButton?: React.ReactNode` and `stripeCheckout?: React.ReactNode` props. - These still fall back to `MockThirdWebAuth` and `MockStripeCheckout` respectively. **Two-step UI logic:** - **Step 1 (when `!isAuthenticated`):** Show the heading "Sign in to continue reading", the subscription price text, a step indicator (`Step 1 of 2 -- Connect your wallet`), then the auth button. The Stripe section is hidden entirely. Below the auth button, show a small note: "You'll be able to pay after signing in." - **Step 2 (when `isAuthenticated`):** Show a green checkmark with "Signed in as `{truncatedWalletAddress}`", then the heading changes or a new step indicator appears (`Step 2 of 2 -- Complete payment`), then the Stripe checkout section. Include a small "Not you? Sign out" link that could reset the context (for mock mode; for real ThirdWeb the `ConnectButton` handles disconnect). - **Remove** the "Already a member? Sign in" text and the "or" divider -- these no longer apply because auth and payment are sequential, not parallel options. **Transition polish:** Consider a simple CSS transition or conditional rendering. No animation library needed -- just `{isAuthenticated ? <Step2 /> : <Step1 />}`. **What stays the same:** The outer container styling (absolute positioning, gradient, card with backdrop blur, shadow, rounded corners). The heading font family. The footer text about cancellation/Stripe. --- ### Step 5: Update MockStripeCheckout **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/paywall/MockStripeCheckout.tsx` **Current behavior:** Static card form with Apple Pay/Google Pay buttons. Subscribe button shows an alert. **Changes:** - Import `useMembership` from context. - On the "Subscribe" button click, instead of calling `alert()`, call `setPaymentStatus("processing")`, wait briefly with a `setTimeout` (e.g., 1.5 seconds for visual feedback), then call `setPaymentStatus("succeeded")`. This simulates a successful payment. - While `paymentStatus === "processing"`, show "Processing..." text on the button and disable it (similar to the real `StripeCheckout`'s loading state). - Apply the same treatment to the Apple Pay and Google Pay buttons -- clicking them triggers the same mock flow. **What stays the same:** The card form inputs and their local state, the visual layout, all styling. --- ### Step 6: Update StripeCheckout (Real SDK) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/paywall/StripeCheckout.tsx` **Current behavior:** Uses `stripe.confirmPayment()` with a redirect to `/demo?success=true`. No context interaction. **Changes:** - Import `useMembership` from context. - In `handleSubmit`, before calling `stripe.confirmPayment()`, call `setPaymentStatus("processing")`. - **Important architectural decision about redirect vs. no-redirect:** Currently the real Stripe flow redirects to `/demo?success=true`. This is a problem because the redirect loses React state (the wallet address in context, the payment status). Two options: **Option A (recommended): Switch to no-redirect confirmation.** Use `stripe.confirmPayment()` with `redirect: "if_required"` instead of always redirecting. If the payment succeeds without redirect (card payments), call `setPaymentStatus("succeeded")` directly. If the payment method requires redirect (e.g., bank redirects), let it redirect and handle success on return via URL params (see demo page changes). **Option B: Keep redirect, restore state from URL.** On the demo page, read `?success=true` from the URL and set `paymentStatus` to `"succeeded"` in context on mount. This is simpler but loses the wallet address context on redirect. Would need to persist wallet address in `sessionStorage` or URL params. **Recommendation: Option A.** The code change is minimal: ```typescript const { error, paymentIntent } = await stripe.confirmPayment({ elements, confirmParams: { return_url: `${window.location.origin}/demo?success=true`, }, redirect: "if_required", }); if (error) { setMessage(error.message || "Payment failed"); setPaymentStatus("failed"); } else if (paymentIntent?.status === "succeeded") { setPaymentStatus("succeeded"); } ``` - Apply the same change to the `ExpressCheckoutElement`'s `onConfirm` handler. **What stays the same:** The `PaymentElement`, `ExpressCheckoutElement` usage, the form structure, the button styling. --- ### Step 7: Update StripeProvider (Pass Wallet Address to API) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/providers/StripeProvider.tsx` **Current behavior:** Calls `/api/stripe/create-payment-intent` on mount (no body), wraps children in `<Elements>`. **Changes:** - Import `useMembership` from context. - Read `walletAddress` from context. - **Change the `useEffect` dependency:** Currently it runs once on mount (`[]`). Change it to depend on `walletAddress`. The intent should only be created once the wallet address is available (since the whole point is to include it in metadata). So: - If `walletAddress` is `null`, do not fetch -- render children without the `<Elements>` wrapper (same as the current error/loading fallback). - When `walletAddress` becomes non-null, fetch the payment intent with the wallet address in the request body. - Update the fetch call to include `walletAddress` in the POST body: ```typescript fetch("/api/stripe/create-payment-intent", { method: "POST", headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" }, body: JSON.stringify({ walletAddress }), }) ``` - Add `walletAddress` to the `useEffect` dependency array. Use a ref or state guard to avoid creating multiple payment intents if the wallet address somehow changes. **What stays the same:** The `Elements` wrapping, the appearance options, the error handling pattern, the Stripe promise loading. --- ### Step 8: Update API Route (Accept Wallet Address in Metadata) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts` **Current behavior:** Creates a PaymentIntent with `metadata: { type: "subscription_demo" }`. Does not read the request body. **Changes:** - Parse the request body to extract `walletAddress`: ```typescript const body = await request.json().catch(() => ({})); const walletAddress = body.walletAddress || "unknown"; ``` - Include `walletAddress` in the PaymentIntent metadata: ```typescript metadata: { type: "subscription_demo", walletAddress, mintNft: "true", // flag for webhook to trigger NFT mint } ``` - Update the function signature from `POST()` to `POST(request: Request)` to access the body. **Why this matters:** A Stripe webhook listening for `payment_intent.succeeded` events can read `metadata.walletAddress` and `metadata.mintNft` to trigger an NFT membership mint to that wallet. The webhook itself is out of scope for this plan but the metadata enables it. **What stays the same:** The secret key check, the amount (999 = $9.99), the currency, automatic_payment_methods, the error handling, the response format. --- ### Step 9: Update BlogPost (Read Context for Unlock) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/blog/BlogPost.tsx` **Current behavior:** Server-compatible component. If `post.isPremium`, always clips content and shows `PaywallOverlay`. No unlock mechanism. **Changes:** - This component must become a `"use client"` component because it needs to read `useMembership()` context for the `isUnlocked` state. Add `"use client"` at the top. - Import `useMembership` from context. - Read `isUnlocked` from context. - The content clipping logic changes from: ``` post.isPremium ? "max-h-[600px] overflow-hidden" : "" ``` to: ``` (post.isPremium && !isUnlocked) ? "max-h-[600px] overflow-hidden" : "" ``` - The `PaywallOverlay` rendering changes from: ``` {post.isPremium && <PaywallOverlay ... />} ``` to: ``` {post.isPremium && !isUnlocked && <PaywallOverlay ... />} ``` - **Remove the `stripeCheckout` and `authButton` props** from `BlogPostProps` since `PaywallOverlay` will render its own components and read from context. The interface simplifies to `{ post: Post; paragraphs: string[] }`. **Unlock transition:** When `isUnlocked` flips to `true`, the overlay disappears and the `max-h-[600px]` constraint is removed, revealing the full article. For a polished feel, consider adding a CSS transition on `max-height` (e.g., `transition-all duration-700`) and a success banner that briefly appears ("Payment successful -- enjoy your article!") before fading. **What stays the same:** The header section (title, excerpt, premium badge, author badge), the paragraph rendering, the article container styling. --- ### Step 10: Update Demo Page (Wire Up Providers and Context) **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/demo/page.tsx` **Current behavior:** Server component. Renders `<BlogPost>` with demo data and no props for stripe/auth (so mocks are used internally by PaywallOverlay). **Changes:** - This must become a `"use client"` component (or wrap the client tree in a client component). Since it currently exports `metadata`, and `metadata` export is not allowed in client components, there are two approaches: **Option A (recommended): Keep the page as a server component, extract a client wrapper.** Create the provider wrapping inline or import a small client component: ```tsx // page.tsx stays as server component with metadata export import DemoContent from "./DemoContent"; export const metadata = { ... }; export default function DemoPage() { return <DemoContent />; } ``` But this means creating yet another file. A simpler approach: **Option B: Move metadata to a `layout.tsx` for the demo route.** This is heavier than needed. **Option C (simplest): Remove the metadata export and make it a client component.** The metadata is just a page title -- not critical for a demo page. **Recommendation: Option A** -- keep the server component for metadata, create a new client component `DemoContent` in the same directory. Actually, to minimize new files, we can just create `DemoContent` as a named export in the same file... but Next.js App Router requires pages to be default exports and you cannot mix server/client in one file. So we need a new file. **New file:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/demo/DemoContent.tsx` This file is `"use client"` and contains the provider wrapping: ```tsx "use client"; import { MembershipProvider } from "@/app/components/providers/MembershipContext"; import ThirdWebProviderWrapper from "@/app/components/providers/ThirdWebProvider"; import BlogPost from "@/app/components/blog/BlogPost"; import { DEMO_POST, DEMO_ARTICLE_PARAGRAPHS } from "@/app/lib/constants"; export default function DemoContent() { return ( <MembershipProvider> <ThirdWebProviderWrapper> <BlogPost post={DEMO_POST} paragraphs={DEMO_ARTICLE_PARAGRAPHS} /> </ThirdWebProviderWrapper> </MembershipProvider> ); } ``` - Update `page.tsx` to import and render `<DemoContent />`. **Provider nesting order (outermost to innermost):** 1. `MembershipProvider` -- must be outermost so all children can read/write membership state. 2. `ThirdWebProviderWrapper` -- ThirdWeb's `useActiveAccount()` needs to be inside this. The `ThirdWebAuth` component uses this hook to push wallet address into membership context. 3. `BlogPost` -- reads `isUnlocked` from context, renders `PaywallOverlay`. 4. Inside `PaywallOverlay`: `ThirdWebAuth` (or `MockThirdWebAuth`) reads/writes context; `StripeProvider` wraps `StripeCheckout` (or `MockStripeCheckout` reads/writes context). **Note on StripeProvider placement:** `StripeProvider` should NOT be at the top level anymore. It should only mount when the user is authenticated (since it needs the wallet address to create the payment intent). The best place for it is inside `PaywallOverlay`, wrapping only the Stripe checkout section, and only rendered in Step 2 (when `isAuthenticated` is true). This has the additional benefit of not creating a payment intent until the user has signed in, saving unnecessary API calls. This means `PaywallOverlay` will import `StripeProvider` and `StripeCheckout` (or their mock equivalents) directly, which is a change from the current prop-injection pattern. This is acceptable because the mock/real decision is already handled inside each component (ThirdWebAuth falls back to mock, StripeCheckout could do the same with a wrapper). **Revised PaywallOverlay Step 2 rendering:** ```tsx {isAuthenticated && ( <StripeProviderConditional> <StripeCheckoutConditional /> </StripeProviderConditional> )} ``` Where `StripeProviderConditional` checks `hasStripeKey()` and either wraps in real `StripeProvider` or renders mock children directly. Actually, the simpler pattern already exists: `StripeProvider` renders children without `<Elements>` when Stripe is not configured (it falls through on the `if (error || !stripe || !clientSecret)` check). And `StripeCheckout` could fall back to `MockStripeCheckout` when `useStripe()` returns null. But currently `StripeCheckout` expects to be inside `<Elements>` -- calling `useStripe()` outside of `<Elements>` throws. **Better approach:** Create a small wrapper component (or keep it inside PaywallOverlay's logic): - Import `hasStripeKey` from `@/app/lib/stripe`. - If `hasStripeKey()`, render `<StripeProvider><StripeCheckout /></StripeProvider>`. - Otherwise, render `<MockStripeCheckout />`. This keeps the mock/real branching clean and avoids the hook-outside-provider problem. --- ### Step 11: Handle Success URL Fallback **File:** `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/demo/DemoContent.tsx` (the new client component) For the case where real Stripe payment requires a redirect (some payment methods), handle the `?success=true` URL parameter: ```tsx import { useSearchParams } from "next/navigation"; export default function DemoContent() { const searchParams = useSearchParams(); const redirectSuccess = searchParams.get("success") === "true"; return ( <MembershipProvider initialUnlocked={redirectSuccess}> ... </MembershipProvider> ); } ``` Add an `initialUnlocked` prop to `MembershipProvider` that, if `true`, sets `paymentStatus` to `"succeeded"` on mount. This handles the redirect return path gracefully. --- ### Summary of All File Changes | # | File | Action | Key Change | |---|------|--------|------------| | 1 | `src/app/components/providers/MembershipContext.tsx` | **CREATE** | React Context for walletAddress, paymentStatus, isUnlocked | | 2 | `src/app/demo/DemoContent.tsx` | **CREATE** | Client component wrapping providers + BlogPost | | 3 | `src/app/components/auth/MockThirdWebAuth.tsx` | MODIFY | Write fake wallet address to context on click | | 4 | `src/app/components/auth/ThirdWebAuth.tsx` | MODIFY | Sync `useActiveAccount()` to context via useEffect | | 5 | `src/app/components/paywall/PaywallOverlay.tsx` | MODIFY | Two-step UI: auth first, payment second (driven by context) | | 6 | `src/app/components/paywall/MockStripeCheckout.tsx` | MODIFY | Write paymentStatus to context on click | | 7 | `src/app/components/paywall/StripeCheckout.tsx` | MODIFY | Use `redirect: "if_required"`, write paymentStatus to context | | 8 | `src/app/components/providers/StripeProvider.tsx` | MODIFY | Accept walletAddress from context, pass in POST body, gate on auth | | 9 | `src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts` | MODIFY | Parse body for walletAddress, add to metadata with mintNft flag | | 10 | `src/app/components/blog/BlogPost.tsx` | MODIFY | Add "use client", read isUnlocked from context, conditionally show overlay | | 11 | `src/app/demo/page.tsx` | MODIFY | Import and render DemoContent instead of BlogPost directly | --- ### Implementation Order and Dependencies The implementation should proceed in this order to maintain a buildable state at each step: 1. **MembershipContext.tsx** (new) -- No dependencies, everything else depends on this. 2. **MockThirdWebAuth.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext. Testable immediately in isolation. 3. **MockStripeCheckout.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext. Testable immediately. 4. **ThirdWebAuth.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext. Needs ThirdWeb env var to test real flow. 5. **StripeProvider.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext. Defers fetch until walletAddress available. 6. **API route** -- Independent of frontend context. Can be tested via curl. 7. **StripeCheckout.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext and updated StripeProvider. 8. **PaywallOverlay.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext and all auth/checkout components being context-aware. 9. **BlogPost.tsx** -- Depends on MembershipContext. 10. **DemoContent.tsx** (new) -- Depends on all of the above. 11. **Demo page.tsx** -- Trivial change, import DemoContent. --- ### Potential Challenges 1. **BlogPost becoming a client component:** Currently BlogPost is a server component (no `"use client"` directive). Making it a client component is fine for the demo page, but if BlogPost is used elsewhere with server rendering, this could be a problem. Mitigation: The demo page is the only consumer, and `DEMO_POST`/`DEMO_ARTICLE_PARAGRAPHS` are static constants, so there is no SSR data-fetching concern. 2. **StripeProvider creating multiple PaymentIntents:** If the user signs in, signs out, and signs back in, the `useEffect` in StripeProvider would fire again. Mitigation: Add a ref (`intentCreated.current`) to track whether a payment intent was already created, and skip the fetch on subsequent calls. Or use an `AbortController` and cleanup. 3. **Real ThirdWeb + context sync timing:** The `useActiveAccount()` hook may not be immediately available on mount. The `useEffect` handles this naturally since it fires when `account` changes. No issue expected. 4. **Stripe redirect payment methods:** Some payment methods (iDEAL, Bancontact, etc.) force a redirect. With `redirect: "if_required"`, these still redirect. The `initialUnlocked` prop on MembershipProvider handles the return. However, the wallet address is lost on redirect. Mitigation: For the MVP, card payments (the most common) do not redirect and work fully in-context. For redirect payment methods, the success page detects `?success=true` and unlocks -- the wallet address was already sent to Stripe in the PaymentIntent metadata, so the webhook still has it for minting. 5. **`useSearchParams` requires Suspense boundary:** In Next.js App Router, `useSearchParams()` in a client component requires a `<Suspense>` boundary. The `DemoContent` component should be wrapped in `<Suspense>` in the page, or `useSearchParams` should be called in a child component wrapped in Suspense. --- ### Critical Files for Implementation - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/providers/MembershipContext.tsx` - New file: the central React Context that coordinates auth state, payment status, and content unlock across all components - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/paywall/PaywallOverlay.tsx` - Most significant UI restructure: converts from parallel auth/pay layout to sequential two-step flow driven by context state - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/blog/BlogPost.tsx` - Must become a client component and read isUnlocked from context to conditionally remove the content clip and overlay - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts` - Must accept wallet address in request body and include it in PaymentIntent metadata (enables downstream NFT minting via webhook) - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/demo/page.tsx` - Entry point that must wire up the correct provider nesting order (MembershipProvider > ThirdWebProvider > BlogPost) agentId: ae3a55ce6630e3977 (use SendMessage with to: 'ae3a55ce6630e3977' to continue this agent) <usage>total_tokens: 41452 tool_uses: 22 duration_ms: 173750</usage>

Input{ "file_path": "/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/node_modules/next/dist/docs/01-app/01-getting-started/15-route-handlers.md", "limit": 80 }
Result 1→--- 2→title: Route Handlers 3→nav_title: Route Handlers 4→description: Learn how to use Route Handlers 5→related: 6→ title: API Reference 7→ description: Learn more about Route Handlers 8→ links: 9→ - app/api-reference/file-conventions/route 10→ - app/guides/backend-for-frontend 11→--- 12→ 13→## Route Handlers 14→ 15→Route Handlers allow you to create custom request handlers for a given route using the Web [Request](https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/API/Request) and [Response](https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/API/Response) APIs. 16→ 17→<Image 18→ alt="Route.js Special File" 19→ srcLight="/docs/light/route-special-file.png" 20→ srcDark="/docs/dark/route-special-file.png" 21→ width="1600" 22→ height="444" 23→/> 24→ 25→> **Good to know**: Route Handlers are only available inside the `app` directory. They are the equivalent of [API Routes](/docs/pages/building-your-application/routing/api-routes) inside the `pages` directory meaning you **do not** need to use API Routes and Route Handlers together. 26→ 27→### Convention 28→ 29→Route Handlers are defined in a [`route.js|ts` file](/docs/app/api-reference/file-conventions/route) inside the `app` directory: 30→ 31→```ts filename="app/api/route.ts" switcher 32→export async function GET(request: Request) {} 33→``` 34→ 35→```js filename="app/api/route.js" switcher 36→export async function GET(request) {} 37→``` 38→ 39→Route Handlers can be nested anywhere inside the `app` directory, similar to `page.js` and `layout.js`. But there **cannot** be a `route.js` file at the same route segment level as `page.js`. 40→ 41→### Supported HTTP Methods 42→ 43→The following [HTTP methods](https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/HTTP/Methods) are supported: `GET`, `POST`, `PUT`, `PATCH`, `DELETE`, `HEAD`, and `OPTIONS`. If an unsupported method is called, Next.js will return a `405 Method Not Allowed` response. 44→ 45→### Extended `NextRequest` and `NextResponse` APIs 46→ 47→In addition to supporting the native [Request](https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/API/Request) and [Response](https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/API/Response) APIs, Next.js extends them with [`NextRequest`](/docs/app/api-reference/functions/next-request) and [`NextResponse`](/docs/app/api-reference/functions/next-response) to provide convenient helpers for advanced use cases. 48→ 49→### Caching 50→ 51→Route Handlers are not cached by default. You can, however, opt into caching for `GET` methods. Other supported HTTP methods are **not** cached. To cache a `GET` method, use a [route config option](/docs/app/guides/caching-without-cache-components#dynamic) such as `export const dynamic = 'force-static'` in your Route Handler file. 52→ 53→```ts filename="app/items/route.ts" switcher 54→export const dynamic = 'force-static' 55→ 56→export async function GET() { 57→ const res = await fetch('https://data.mongodb-api.com/...', { 58→ headers: { 59→ 'Content-Type': 'application/json', 60→ 'API-Key': process.env.DATA_API_KEY, 61→ }, 62→ }) 63→ const data = await res.json() 64→ 65→ return Response.json({ data }) 66→} 67→``` 68→ 69→```js filename="app/items/route.js" switcher 70→export const dynamic = 'force-static' 71→ 72→export async function GET() { 73→ const res = await fetch('https://data.mongodb-api.com/...', { 74→ headers: { 75→ 'Content-Type': 'application/json', 76→ 'API-Key': process.env.DATA_API_KEY, 77→ }, 78→ }) 79→ const data = await res.json() 80→ <system-reminder> Whenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior. </system-reminder>

Assistant16:09:19
We don't have either of those things. Here's what actually exists: **Payment:** The Stripe integration is a one-time `PaymentIntent` for $9.99 — not a recurring subscription. There's no `Subscription` object, no `price_id`, and no webhook endpoint (`/api/stripe/webhook` doesn't exist). The "Subscribe" button label is aspirational; the backend creates a single charge. **Smart contract:** There's no smart contract, no NFT minting logic, and no on-chain interaction. The `mintNft: "true"` metadata we just added to the PaymentIntent is a breadcrumb for a future webhook handler to trigger minting — but that handler doesn't exist yet. ThirdWeb is used solely for wallet authentication (social login via `inAppWallet`), not for any blockchain transactions. **What's actually wired up end-to-end:** 1. User signs in (wallet address captured via ThirdWeb or mock) 2. Wallet address is stored in `MembershipContext` and sent to the PaymentIntent as metadata 3. Payment succeeds → `paymentStatus` flips to `"succeeded"` in React state → article unlocks client-side 4. No server-side verification, no persistent unlock, no webhook, no NFT mint To make the plan in the metadata real, you'd need: - A Stripe webhook route listening for `payment_intent.succeeded` - That handler reads `walletAddress` + `mintNft` from the event metadata - It calls a ThirdWeb Engine endpoint (or direct contract call) to mint a membership NFT to that wallet - For recurring payments, switch from `PaymentIntent` to a Stripe `Subscription` with a `Price` Want me to build any of those?

ResultNow I have all the information I need. Let me produce the detailed implementation plan. --- ## Implementation Plan: Stripe Subscriptions + Webhook + ThirdWeb NFT Minting ### Architecture Overview The plan converts the existing one-time PaymentIntent flow to a Stripe recurring Subscription flow while preserving the client-side Elements integration. A new webhook endpoint handles `invoice.payment_succeeded` events and triggers NFT minting via the ThirdWeb Engine REST API. The mock path remains untouched. --- ### 1. New Environment Variables Add to `.env.local.example` (and document in README): ``` # Stripe (existing) NEXT_PUBLIC_STRIPE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY= STRIPE_SECRET_KEY= # Stripe Webhook (new) STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET= # ThirdWeb Engine (new) THIRDWEB_ENGINE_URL= THIRDWEB_ENGINE_ACCESS_TOKEN= THIRDWEB_ENGINE_BACKEND_WALLET= NFT_CONTRACT_ADDRESS= NFT_CHAIN_ID= ``` All new variables are server-only (no `NEXT_PUBLIC_` prefix), so they are never exposed to the browser. --- ### 2. File-by-File Changes #### FILE 1 (MODIFY): `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts` **Rename directory** to `create-subscription` (path becomes `src/app/api/stripe/create-subscription/route.ts`). Alternatively, keep the same path but completely rewrite the body. Renaming is cleaner since the semantics change. The old path can be deleted. **New path**: `src/app/api/stripe/create-subscription/route.ts` **What it does**: - Accepts `POST` with `{ walletAddress }` in the JSON body (same contract as before). - Instantiates the Stripe SDK from `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`. - **Find-or-create Product**: Calls `stripe.products.list({ limit: 1 })` filtering by a known metadata key (e.g., `metadata: { app: "paywall-times" }`) or uses `stripe.products.search` with a query on metadata. Simpler approach: always use a fixed lookup_key on the Price. The Product is created once if not found. - **Find-or-create Price**: Calls `stripe.prices.list({ lookup_keys: ["paywall_times_monthly"] })`. If empty, creates a new Product and Price: ``` product = stripe.products.create({ name: "Paywall Times Monthly", metadata: { app: "paywall_times" } }) price = stripe.prices.create({ unit_amount: 999, currency: "usd", recurring: { interval: "month" }, product: product.id, lookup_key: "paywall_times_monthly" }) ``` - **Find-or-create Customer**: Calls `stripe.customers.list({ limit: 1, email: undefined })` -- since we only have a wallet address and no email, we search by metadata: `stripe.customers.search({ query: 'metadata["walletAddress"]:"0x..."' })`. If not found, creates a new Customer with `metadata: { walletAddress }`. - **Create Subscription**: ``` stripe.subscriptions.create({ customer: customer.id, items: [{ price: price.id }], payment_behavior: "default_incomplete", payment_settings: { save_default_payment_method: "on_subscription" }, metadata: { walletAddress, mintNft: "true" }, expand: ["latest_invoice"], }) ``` - **Extract client_secret**: The expanded `latest_invoice` is a `Stripe.Invoice` object. In Stripe v20 (`2026-02-25.clover`), use `(subscription.latest_invoice as Stripe.Invoice).confirmation_secret?.client_secret`. If that field is not present (edge case), fall back to looking up the PaymentIntent via `stripe.invoices.retrieve(invoiceId, { expand: ["payments"] })`. - **Return**: `{ clientSecret, subscriptionId }`. **Key implementation detail for Stripe v20**: The Invoice object no longer has a top-level `payment_intent` field. Instead it has `confirmation_secret.client_secret` which provides the PaymentIntent client secret needed by the Elements flow on the frontend. The subscription metadata (including `walletAddress` and `mintNft`) is snapshotted onto the invoice at `invoice.parent.subscription_details.metadata`. #### FILE 2 (NEW): `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/webhook/route.ts` **What it does**: - Exports `POST(request: Request)` -- a Next.js 16 route handler. - Reads the raw body via `request.text()` (important: must not use `request.json()` before signature verification). - Reads `stripe-signature` header from `request.headers.get("stripe-signature")`. - Verifies the event: `stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(rawBody, sigHeader, process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET!)`. - Dispatches on `event.type`: - **`invoice.payment_succeeded`**: - Extract the invoice object: `event.data.object` as `Stripe.Invoice`. - Get subscription metadata from `invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.metadata`. - If `metadata?.mintNft === "true"` and `metadata?.walletAddress`, call the NFT mint helper (imported from a shared lib). - If subscription details are not directly on the invoice (for older invoices), fall back to `stripe.subscriptions.retrieve(invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.subscription)` to get metadata. - **`customer.subscription.deleted`** (optional): Log the cancellation. Could be used later for revoking access. - Returns `new Response(JSON.stringify({ received: true }), { status: 200 })`. - On signature verification failure, returns 400. - On any processing error, returns 500 but still acknowledges receipt (to prevent Stripe retries for non-transient errors). **Critical**: This route must NOT parse the body as JSON before signature verification. The `request.text()` approach is correct per the Next.js 16 docs (which show exactly this webhook pattern). #### FILE 3 (NEW): `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/lib/thirdweb-engine.ts` **What it does**: - Server-only module (no `"use client"` directive, no `NEXT_PUBLIC_` env vars). - Exports `mintMembershipNFT(walletAddress: string): Promise<{ success: boolean; transactionHash?: string; error?: string }>`. - Reads env vars: `THIRDWEB_ENGINE_URL`, `THIRDWEB_ENGINE_ACCESS_TOKEN`, `THIRDWEB_ENGINE_BACKEND_WALLET`, `NFT_CONTRACT_ADDRESS`, `NFT_CHAIN_ID`. - Makes a `POST` request to `{THIRDWEB_ENGINE_URL}/contract/{NFT_CHAIN_ID}/{NFT_CONTRACT_ADDRESS}/erc721/mint-to` with: - Headers: `Authorization: Bearer ${THIRDWEB_ENGINE_ACCESS_TOKEN}`, `Content-Type: application/json`, `x-backend-wallet-address: ${THIRDWEB_ENGINE_BACKEND_WALLET}`. - Body: `{ "receiver": walletAddress, "metadata": { "name": "Paywall Times Membership", "description": "Monthly membership NFT for The Paywall Times", "image": "" } }`. - Returns the parsed response. Detailed API Route Logic: `create-payment-intent/route.ts` (Rewritten) ``` POST /api/stripe/create-payment-intent Body: { walletAddress: string } Response: { clientSecret: string; subscriptionId: string } ``` **Algorithm**: 1. Validate `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` exists (existing pattern). 2. Parse `walletAddress` from body (existing pattern). 3. Instantiate `new Stripe(secretKey)`. 4. **Find or create Price**: - `const prices = await stripe.prices.list({ lookup_keys: ["paywall_times_monthly"], limit: 1 })` - If `prices.data.length === 0`: - `const product = await stripe.products.create({ name: "Paywall Times Monthly Membership" })` - `const price = await stripe.prices.create({ product: product.id, unit_amount: 999, currency: "usd", recurring: { interval: "month" }, lookup_key: "paywall_times_monthly" })` - Else: `const price = prices.data[0]` 5. **Find or create Customer** (keyed by walletAddress): - `const customers = await stripe.customers.search({ query: 'metadata["walletAddress"]:"' + walletAddress + '"', limit: 1 })` - If none found: `const customer = await stripe.customers.create({ metadata: { walletAddress } })` - Else: `const customer = customers.data[0]` 6. **Check for existing active subscription** (prevent duplicates): - `const subs = await stripe.subscriptions.list({ customer: customer.id, status: "active", limit: 1 })` - If active sub exists, could either return its existing client secret or create a new one. For simplicity, always create a new subscription (Stripe allows multiple). - Better: check for `incomplete` subscriptions too and reuse them. - Simplest safe approach: `const subs = await stripe.subscriptions.list({ customer: customer.id, limit: 1, status: "incomplete" })` -- if found, retrieve and return its latest invoice client secret. Otherwise create new. 7. **Create Subscription**: ``` const subscription = await stripe.subscriptions.create({ customer: customer.id, items: [{ price: price.id }], payment_behavior: "default_incomplete", payment_settings: { save_default_payment_method: "on_subscription" }, metadata: { walletAddress, mintNft: "true" }, expand: ["latest_invoice"], }) ``` 8. **Extract clientSecret**: ``` const invoice = subscription.latest_invoice as Stripe.Invoice; const clientSecret = invoice.confirmation_secret?.client_secret; ``` 9. Return `{ clientSecret, subscriptionId: subscription.id }`. --- ### 5. Detailed Webhook Logic: `webhook/route.ts` ``` POST /api/stripe/webhook Headers: stripe-signature Body: raw event payload Response: { received: true } ``` **Algorithm**: 1. Read `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` and `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET` from env. 2. `const rawBody = await request.text()`. 3. `const sigHeader = request.headers.get("stripe-signature")`. 4. Guard: if no `sigHeader` or no `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`, return 400. 5. `const event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(rawBody, sigHeader, STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET)` -- wrapped in try/catch; return 400 on `StripeSignatureVerificationError`. 6. Switch on `event.type`: - `"invoice.payment_succeeded"`: - `const invoice = event.data.object as Stripe.Invoice` - `const metadata = invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.metadata` - If `metadata?.mintNft === "true"` and `metadata?.walletAddress`: - Call `mintMembershipNFT(metadata.walletAddress)` - Log result - If metadata is null/missing (safety net): retrieve subscription directly via `stripe.subscriptions.retrieve(invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.subscription as string)` and read metadata from there. - `"customer.subscription.deleted"`: - Log: `console.log("Subscription cancelled:", event.data.object.id)` - (Future: could call a revoke/burn NFT endpoint) 7. Return `new Response(JSON.stringify({ received: true }), { status: 200 })`. --- ### 6. How the Mock Path Continues to Work The mock path is gated by `hasStripeKey()` in `PaywallOverlay.tsx` (line 13). When `NEXT_PUBLIC_STRIPE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY` is not set: - `hasStripeKey()` returns `false` - `PaywallOverlay` renders `<MockStripeCheckout />` instead of `<StripeProvider><StripeCheckout /></StripeProvider>` - `MockStripeCheckout` never calls any API endpoint -- it directly calls `setPaymentStatus("processing")` then `setPaymentStatus("succeeded")` after a timeout - No changes are made to `MockStripeCheckout.tsx` or `PaywallOverlay.tsx` The mock path is **completely untouched** by this plan. The conditional branching at the `PaywallOverlay` level ensures that the subscription API route is never called when Stripe keys are absent. --- ### 7. Potential Challenges and Mitigations **Challenge 1: `confirmation_secret` might not be populated on the initial invoice.** The `confirmation_secret` field is documented as optional (`?`). If Stripe returns `null` for this on a just-created subscription with `payment_behavior: "default_incomplete"`, we need a fallback. Mitigation: after creating the subscription, if `confirmation_secret` is null, retrieve the invoice with `expand: ["payments"]` or look up the PaymentIntent via `stripe.invoices.retrieve(invoiceId)`. However, in practice, with `payment_behavior: "default_incomplete"`, the invoice is always finalized with a PaymentIntent, so `confirmation_secret` should always be populated. **Challenge 2: `stripe.customers.search` has eventual consistency.** Stripe Search API may not immediately return a just-created customer. Mitigation: use `stripe.customers.list` with `metadata` filtering if `search` proves unreliable, or simply always create a new customer (accepting potential duplicates). A pragmatic alternative: hash the wallet address and use it as a deterministic idempotency key for customer creation, catching "customer already exists" errors. **Challenge 3: Webhook idempotency for NFT minting.** Stripe may deliver the same webhook event more than once. If the NFT mint is called twice for the same invoice, two NFTs could be minted. Mitigation: Before minting, check the invoice ID. Since there's no database, store the invoice ID in the subscription metadata after a successful mint by updating the subscription: `stripe.subscriptions.update(subId, { metadata: { lastMintedInvoice: invoiceId } })`. On subsequent webhook deliveries, check if `lastMintedInvoice === invoiceId` and skip. **Challenge 4: ThirdWeb Engine availability.** The Engine REST API might be down or slow. Mitigation: The webhook handler should not block on a slow Engine call. Wrap the mint call in a timeout. If it fails, log the error. Stripe will retry the webhook, giving another chance to mint. Alternatively, return 200 to Stripe immediately and log the failure for manual retry. --- ### Critical Files for Implementation - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/create-payment-intent/route.ts` - Core file to rewrite: replaces PaymentIntent creation with Subscription creation, find-or-create Product/Price/Customer logic - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/api/stripe/webhook/route.ts` - New file: webhook handler for signature verification, event dispatch, and triggering NFT mint on `invoice.payment_succeeded` - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/lib/thirdweb-engine.ts` - New file: server-side utility for calling ThirdWeb Engine REST API to mint ERC-721 membership NFTs - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/src/app/components/providers/StripeProvider.tsx` - May need URL update if the API route is renamed (not needed if route path is kept unchanged) - `/Users/josephgenest/Desktop/MercorSprint31926/model_b/node_modules/stripe/types/Invoices.d.ts` - Reference file: documents the Stripe v20 Invoice type where `confirmation_secret.client_secret` replaces the old `payment_intent.client_secret` pattern, and `parent.subscription_details.metadata` replaces the old top-level `subscription` field agentId: a50cf6196a08b5b7e (use SendMessage with to: 'a50cf6196a08b5b7e' to continue this agent) <usage>total_tokens: 70654 tool_uses: 53 duration_ms: 262637</usage>

Result 1→# Auth-First Paywall Flow — Restructuring Plan 2→ 3→## Context 4→The current paywall overlay shows sign-in and payment side-by-side, with no connection between them. If a user pays via Stripe without signing in via ThirdWeb, there's no wallet address to mint a membership NFT to. We need to restructure so sign-in happens **before** payment, the wallet address flows into Stripe metadata, and successful payment unlocks the article. 5→ 6→## Approach 7→Introduce a `MembershipContext` (React Context) that tracks wallet address, payment status, and derived unlock state. Restructure the PaywallOverlay into a two-step flow (Step 1: sign in, Step 2: pay). Mock components interact with context so the full flow works without env vars. 8→ 9→## File Changes 10→ 11→### 1.
