User (Turn 12)16:33:06
Walk me through the full user experience on the back end?
Assistant16:33:32
Sure. Here's the end-to-end backend flow when a real user subscribes: ### 1. User clicks "Subscribe" → `POST /api/stripe/create-payment-intent` The frontend sends `{ walletAddress }` to this endpoint. The route does three find-or-create operations in sequence: - **Price**: Looks up a recurring $9.99/mo price by the key `paywall_times_monthly`. If it doesn't exist yet (first-ever subscriber), it creates the Product + Price on the fly. (`route.ts:28-46`) - **Customer**: Searches Stripe for an existing customer whose metadata contains this `walletAddress`. If none found, creates one. (`route.ts:49-60`) - **Subscription**: Checks if this customer already has an `incomplete` subscription (e.g. they started checkout but didn't finish). If so, it returns the existing `clientSecret` to resume — no duplicate subscriptions. (`route.ts:63-78`) If no incomplete subscription exists, it creates a new one with `payment_behavior: "default_incomplete"`. This tells Stripe "create the subscription but don't activate it until the first invoice is paid." The subscription metadata carries `walletAddress` and `mintNft: "true"`. (`route.ts:81-93`) The response extracts `clientSecret` from the subscription's latest invoice `confirmation_secret` and sends it back. The frontend doesn't know or care that this is a subscription — `stripe.confirmPayment()` works identically. ### 2. User enters card details → Stripe processes payment This happens entirely client-side via Stripe Elements. The `clientSecret` ties the payment form to the subscription's first invoice. On success, Stripe transitions the subscription from `incomplete` → `active` and fires events. ### 3. Stripe sends `invoice.payment_succeeded` → `POST /api/stripe/webhook` Stripe POSTs a signed event to the webhook. The handler: 1. **Verifies the signature** using `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET` — rejects tampered or replayed requests. (`webhook/route.ts:26-33`) 2. **Reads subscription metadata** from `invoice.parent.subscription_details.metadata` — this is an immutable snapshot of the subscription's metadata at invoice finalization time. (`webhook/route.ts:37-38`) 3. **Checks `mintNft === "true"` and `walletAddress` is present**. If the subscription wasn't set up for minting (no wallet), it does nothing. (`webhook/route.ts:40`) 4. **Idempotency check**: Retrieves the subscription and compares `metadata.lastMintedInvoice` against the current invoice ID. If they match, this is a replay — skip. (`webhook/route.ts:49-52`) 5. **Calls `mintMembershipNFT(walletAddress)`**: This POSTs to ThirdWeb Engine's `/contract/{chain}/{address}/erc721/mint-to`, passing the user's wallet as receiver and membership metadata. The backend wallet (configured via env var) pays gas. (`thirdweb-engine.ts:28-45`) 6. **On success**: Updates the subscription's metadata with `lastMintedInvoice: invoice.id`, closing the idempotency loop for this billing cycle. (`webhook/route.ts:61-63`) ### 4. Next month — automatic renewal Stripe automatically invoices the customer each month. When the renewal payment succeeds, Stripe fires `invoice.payment_succeeded` again. The webhook runs the same flow — idempotency check passes (different invoice ID), so a new membership NFT is minted for that billing cycle. ### 5. Cancellation → `customer.subscription.deleted` If the subscription is cancelled, the webhook logs it. This is a placeholder for future NFT revocation logic. (`webhook/route.ts:69-74`) ### Failure modes - **ThirdWeb Engine not configured**: The webhook logs a warning and returns 200 — Stripe won't retry, and no mint happens. This is expected in dev without Engine credentials. - **Mint fails**: Logged as an error, `lastMintedInvoice` is *not* set, so Stripe retries will re-attempt the mint. - **Missing Stripe keys**: The route returns 500 before touching any Stripe API.
User (Turn 13)16:38:06
What do you mean by- Checks mintNft === "true" and walletAddress is present. If the subscription wasn't set up for minting (no wallet), it does nothing. (webhook/route.ts:40) 4. Idempotency check: Retrieves the subscription and compares metadata.lastMintedInvoice against the current invoice ID. If they match, this is a replay — skip. (webhook/route.ts:49-52)
Assistant16:38:18
Good question — let me clarify both. ### `mintNft` / `walletAddress` check The subscription metadata is only populated with `mintNft: "true"` and `walletAddress` when the user provided a wallet address at checkout time (`create-payment-intent/route.ts:88`): ```ts metadata: { ...(walletAddress ? { walletAddress, mintNft: "true" } : {}), }, ``` If someone subscribes without connecting a wallet (i.e. `walletAddress` is `null`), the subscription metadata is empty — no `mintNft`, no `walletAddress`. So when the webhook fires, the check at line 40 sees neither field and skips the entire minting block. The payment still succeeds, the subscription is still active — they just don't get an NFT because there's no wallet to mint to. ### Idempotency check Stripe can deliver the same webhook event more than once — network timeouts, retries, or manual replays from the dashboard. Without protection, we'd mint duplicate NFTs for the same payment. The guard works like this: 1. After a successful mint, we stamp the subscription metadata with `lastMintedInvoice: "in_abc123"` (`webhook/route.ts:61-63`) 2. Next time the webhook fires for the same invoice, we retrieve the subscription, see `lastMintedInvoice` already equals this invoice ID, and skip (`webhook/route.ts:49-52`) 3. When the *next month's* invoice arrives, it has a different ID (e.g. `in_def456`), so the check passes and a new NFT is minted It's essentially a "last processed" marker scoped to the subscription, ensuring exactly-once minting per billing cycle.
User (Turn 14)16:38:49
Where is the subscription active?
Assistant16:38:58
It's not in our code — Stripe manages that transition automatically. When we create the subscription with `payment_behavior: "default_incomplete"` (`create-payment-intent/route.ts:84`), Stripe creates it in `incomplete` status with an unpaid first invoice. Once the user completes payment on the frontend via `stripe.confirmPayment()`, Stripe internally flips the subscription to `active`. We never call `stripe.subscriptions.update(id, { status: "active" })` or anything like that. Our backend only observes the result of that transition — the `invoice.payment_succeeded` webhook fires *because* the subscription became active and its first invoice was paid.
User (Turn 15)16:39:20
Ah, so what happens if a recurring payment fails or someone wants to cancel their membership?
Assistant16:39:32
Right now, not much — the implementation is minimal on both fronts. ### Failed recurring payment We don't handle it. Stripe has its own retry logic (Smart Retries — typically 3-4 attempts over a few weeks), and if all retries fail, Stripe eventually marks the subscription as `past_due` or `canceled` depending on your Stripe Dashboard settings. But our webhook only listens for `invoice.payment_succeeded`. There's no handler for `invoice.payment_failed`, so we wouldn't know about it server-side — no email to the user, no access revocation, nothing. ### Cancellation The webhook catches `customer.subscription.deleted` but just logs it (`webhook/route.ts:69-74`): ```ts case "customer.subscription.deleted": { const subscription = event.data.object as Stripe.Subscription; console.log( `Subscription ${subscription.id} cancelled for customer ${subscription.customer}` ); break; } ``` There's no cancel endpoint for the user to call, and no NFT revocation or access removal logic. ### What's missing to make this production-ready - An `invoice.payment_failed` webhook handler to notify the user or flag their account - A `POST /api/stripe/cancel-subscription` endpoint so users can self-service cancel - Access gating tied to subscription status (right now `MembershipContext` just tracks payment completion in local state — it doesn't check whether the subscription is still active) - NFT revocation on cancellation (burn or transfer back) The plan called out the cancellation handler as a "placeholder for future NFT revocation," so this was intentionally deferred.

Result 1→import { NextResponse } from "next/server"; 2→import Stripe from "stripe"; 3→import { mintMembershipNFT, hasThirdWebEngineConfig } from "@/app/lib/thirdweb-engine"; 4→ 5→export async function POST(request: Request) { 6→ const secretKey = process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY; 7→ const webhookSecret = process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET; 8→ 9→ if (!secretKey || !webhookSecret) { 10→ return NextResponse.json( 11→ { error: "Stripe webhook not configured" }, 12→ { status: 500 } 13→ ); 14→ } 15→ 16→ const stripe = new Stripe(secretKey); 17→ 18→ const rawBody = await request.text(); 19→ const sigHeader = request.headers.get("stripe-signature"); 20→ 21→ if (!sigHeader) { 22→ return NextResponse.json({ error: "Missing stripe-signature header" }, { status: 400 }); 23→ } 24→ 25→ let event: Stripe.Event; 26→ try { 27→ event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(rawBody, sigHeader, webhookSecret); 28→ } catch (err) { 29→ const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : "Signature verification failed"; 30→ console.error(`Webhook signature verification failed: ${message}`); 31→ return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 400 }); 32→ } 33→ 34→ switch (event.type) { 35→ case "invoice.payment_succeeded": { 36→ const invoice = event.data.object as Stripe.Invoice; 37→ const metadata = invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.metadata; 38→ 39→ if (metadata?.mintNft === "true" && metadata.walletAddress) { 40→ const subscriptionId = 41→ typeof invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.subscription === "string" 42→ ? invoice.parent.subscription_details.subscription 43→ : invoice.parent?.subscription_details?.subscription?.id; 44→ 45→ if (subscriptionId) { 46→ // Idempotency: check if we already minted for this invoice 47→ const sub = await stripe.subscriptions.retrieve(subscriptionId); 48→ if (sub.metadata.lastMintedInvoice === invoice.id) { 49→ console.log(`Mint already completed for invoice ${invoice.id}, skipping`); 50→ break; 51→ } 52→ 53→ if (!hasThirdWebEngineConfig()) { 54→ console.warn("ThirdWeb Engine not configured — skipping NFT mint"); 55→ break; 56→ } 57→ 58→ console.log(`Minting membership NFT to ${metadata.walletAddress} for invoice ${invoice.id}`); 59→ const result = await mintMembershipNFT(metadata.walletAddress); 60→ 61→ if (result.success) { 62→ console.log(`Mint queued: ${result.queueId}`); 63→ await stripe.subscriptions.update(subscriptionId, { 64→ metadata: { ...sub.metadata, lastMintedInvoice: invoice.id }, 65→ }); 66→ } else { 67→ console.error(`Mint failed: ${result.error}`); 68→ } 69→ } 70→ } 71→ break; 72→ } 73→ 74→ case "customer.subscription.deleted": { 75→ const subscription = event.data.object as Stripe.Subscription; 76→ console.log( 77→ `Subscription ${subscription.id} cancelled for customer ${subscription.customer}` 78→ ); 79→ break; 80→ } 81→ 82→ default: 83→ break; 84→ } 85→ 86→ return NextResponse.json({ received: true }); 87→} 88→ <system-reminder> Whenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Call ThirdWeb Engine from the webhook to mint a membership NFT to the user's wallet 8→ 9→## New Environment Variables 10→All server-only (no `NEXT_PUBLIC_` prefix): 11→``` 12→STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET= # From `stripe listen` or Stripe Dashboard 13→THIRDWEB_ENGINE_URL= # e.g. https://engine.thirdweb.com 14→THIRDWEB_ENGINE_ACCESS_TOKEN= # Engine bearer token 15→THIRDWEB_ENGINE_BACKEND_WALLET= # Server wallet address that pays gas 16→NFT_CONTRACT_ADDRESS= # ERC-721 contract address 17→NFT_CHAIN_ID= # e.g. 84532 (Base Sepolia) 18→``` 19→ 20→## File Changes 21→ 22→### 1. If empty, create Product + Price ($9.99/mo recurring). 33→3. **Find-or-create Customer**: `stripe.customers.search({ query: 'metadata["walletAddress"]:"0x..."' })`. If none, create customer with `metadata: { walletAddress }`. 34→4. **Reuse incomplete subscription**: Check for existing `incomplete` subscription for this customer. If found, return its existing `clientSecret` to avoid duplicates. 35→5. **Create Subscription**: `stripe.subscriptions.create({ customer, items: [{ price }], payment_behavior: "default_incomplete", payment_settings: { save_default_payment_method: "on_subscription" }, metadata: { walletAddress, mintNft: "true" }, expand: ["latest_invoice"] })` 36→6. **Extract clientSecret**: `(subscription.latest_invoice as Stripe.Invoice).confirmation_secret!.client_secret` (Stripe v20 API — confirmed in `node_modules/stripe/types/Invoices.d.ts:164,517-521`) 37→7. Implement the following plan: # Subscription Cancellation + NFT Burn ## Context Users can subscribe but have no way to cancel. The `customer.subscription.deleted` webhook handler is a placeholder that only logs. We need: 1. A cancel API endpoint that sets `cancel_at_period_end: true` (user keeps access until paid-through date) 2. A subscription status API so the frontend knows the subscription state 3. NFT burn via ThirdWeb Engine when the subscription actually ends 4. A cancel button in the UI with confirmation ## File Changes ### 1. MODIFY `src/app/lib/thirdweb-engine.ts` Add `burnMembershipNFT(walletAddress: string)`: - GET `/contract/{chain}/{address}/erc721/get-owned?ownerWallet={wallet}` to find token IDs - If tokens found, POST `/contract/{chain}/{address}/erc721/burn` with the latest token ID - Returns `{ success, queueId?, error? }` - If no tokens found, return success (nothing to burn) ### 2. CREATE `src/app/api/stripe/cancel-subscription/route.ts` POST endpoint, accepts `{ walletAddress }`: 1. Find customer by `stripe.customers.search({ query: 'metadata["walletAddress"]:"0x..."' })` 2. Find their active subscription: `stripe.subscriptions.list({ customer, status: "active", limit: 1 })` 3. If no active subscription, return 404 4. Set `cancel_at_period_end: true`: `stripe.subscriptions.update(subId, { cancel_at_period_end: true })` 5. Return `{ canceledAt, currentPeriodEnd }` (epoch → ISO string for frontend) ### 3. CREATE `src/app/api/stripe/subscription-status/route.ts` GET endpoint, reads `walletAddress` from query param: 1. Find customer by wallet metadata (same search pattern) 2. Find active or `cancel_at_period_end` subscription 3. Return `{ status, cancelAtPeriodEnd, currentPeriodEnd }` or `{ status: "none" }` if no subscription ### 4. MODIFY `src/app/api/stripe/webhook/route.ts` Update `customer.subscription.deleted` handler: - Read `walletAddress` from `subscription.metadata` - If present and ThirdWeb Engine is configured, call `burnMembershipNFT(walletAddress)` - Log success/failure ### 5. CREATE `src/app/components/subscription/SubscriptionManager.tsx` Client component shown below the article when `isUnlocked` is true: - On mount: fetch `GET /api/stripe/subscription-status?walletAddress=...` - Displays subscription status (active, canceling with end date) - "Cancel Subscription" button opens a confirmation dialog (simple inline confirm, not a modal library) - On confirm: POST `/api/stripe/cancel-subscription` with walletAddress - After cancel: updates local state to show "Your subscription ends on {date}" - When mock path (no Stripe keys): don't render anything (no subscription to manage) ### 6. MODIFY `src/app/components/blog/BlogPost.tsx` Render `<SubscriptionManager />` below the article content when `isUnlocked && post.isPremium`. ## Implementation Order 1. `thirdweb-engine.ts` — add `burnMembershipNFT` (no deps) 2. `cancel-subscription/route.ts` (no deps) 3. `subscription-status/route.ts` (no deps) 4. `webhook/route.ts` — update deleted handler (depends on step 1) 5. `SubscriptionManager.tsx` (depends on steps 2-3) 6. `BlogPost.tsx` — render SubscriptionManager (depends on step 5) ## Files NOT Modified - `MembershipContext.tsx` — SubscriptionManager manages its own state - `PaywallOverlay.tsx` — cancel UI is separate from the paywall - `StripeProvider.tsx`, `StripeCheckout.tsx` — unaffected - `.env.local.example` — no new env vars needed ## Verification 1. **Build**: `npx next build` passes 2. **Mock path**: no SubscriptionManager rendered (hasStripeKey() returns false, no subscription to query) 3. **Cancel flow** (with test keys): Subscribe → article unlocks → SubscriptionManager appears → click Cancel → confirm → UI shows "ends on {date}" → Stripe Dashboard shows `cancel_at_period_end: true` 4. **Webhook**: When period ends and Stripe fires `customer.subscription.deleted`, burn is attempted (will log error if Engine not configured) 5. **Status API**: After canceling, `subscription-status` returns `{ status: "active", cancelAtPeriodEnd: true, currentPeriodEnd: "..." }` If you need specific details from before exiting plan mode (like exact code snippets, error messages, or content you generated), read the full transcript at: /Users/josephgenest/.claude/projects/-Users-josephgenest-Desktop-MercorSprint31926-model-b/5c9b5bdf-b263-437f-bf7a-4dd77116cf62.jsonl

Assistant16:59:28
Here's the full membership system walkthrough: --- ## The Paywall Times — Membership System ### Entry Point Everything starts at **`/demo`**. `DemoContent.tsx` wraps the page in two providers: - **`MembershipProvider`** — tracks `walletAddress`, `paymentStatus`, and derived `isUnlocked`/`isAuthenticated` flags. If the URL has `?success=true`, it auto-unlocks (for post-payment redirect). - **`ThirdWebProviderWrapper`** — enables wallet connection (gracefully skipped if no ThirdWeb client ID is configured). It then renders `BlogPost` with a hardcoded premium demo article. --- ### Step 1: Paywall + Wallet Connection **`BlogPost.tsx`** checks `isUnlocked`. If the post is premium and the user hasn't paid: - Content is height-clipped to 600px - **`PaywallOverlay`** renders on top with a two-step flow: **Step 1 — Connect wallet:** `ThirdWebAuth` shows a ThirdWeb `ConnectButton` supporting Google, Apple, Facebook, and email sign-in via `inAppWallet`. On connect, it calls `setWalletAddress()` in context. Falls back to `MockThirdWebAuth` (sets a dummy `0xDEMO...` address) when ThirdWeb isn't configured. **Step 2 — Pay:** Once authenticated, `StripeProvider` kicks in: 1. POSTs to `/api/stripe/create-payment-intent` with the wallet address 2. The API finds/creates a Stripe customer (keyed by `metadata.walletAddress`), finds/creates a $9.99/month recurring price, and returns a `clientSecret` 3. `StripeCheckout` renders Express Checkout + Payment Element, then calls `stripe.confirmPayment()` 4. On success, redirects to `/demo?success=true` → `MembershipProvider` sees the param → `isUnlocked = true` When Stripe keys aren't configured, `MockStripeCheckout` simulates the flow with a 1.5s delay. --- ### Step 2: Webhook — NFT Mint When Stripe confirms the first invoice payment, it fires `invoice.payment_succeeded` to **`/api/stripe/webhook`**: 1. Checks subscription metadata for `mintNft: "true"` and a `walletAddress` 2. Checks idempotency: skips if `lastMintedInvoice` already matches this invoice 3. Calls **`mintMembershipNFT(walletAddress)`** in `thirdweb-engine.ts`, which POSTs to ThirdWeb Engine's `erc721/mint-to` endpoint 4. On success, stamps `lastMintedInvoice` on the subscription metadata The user now has an on-chain ERC-721 "The Paywall Times Membership" NFT. --- ### Step 3: Subscription Management When the article is unlocked (`isUnlocked && post.isPremium`), **`BlogPost.tsx`** renders **`SubscriptionManager`** below the article: 1. On mount, fetches `GET /api/stripe/subscription-status?walletAddress=...` 2. The API looks up the Stripe customer by wallet metadata, finds their active subscription, and returns `{ status, cancelAtPeriodEnd, currentPeriodEnd }` 3. If active: shows next billing date + "Cancel Subscription" button 4. If canceling: shows "Your subscription ends on {date}" Doesn't render at all when Stripe keys aren't configured (mock path). --- ### Step 4: Cancellation When the user clicks Cancel and confirms: 1. `SubscriptionManager` POSTs to `/api/stripe/cancel-subscription` with the wallet address 2. The API finds the customer → finds their active subscription → sets `cancel_at_period_end: true` 3. Returns `{ canceledAt, currentPeriodEnd }` 4. UI updates to show "Your subscription ends on {date}" — access continues until then --- ### Step 5: Webhook — NFT Burn When the subscription period actually ends, Stripe fires `customer.subscription.deleted`: 1. The webhook reads `walletAddress` from subscription metadata 2. Calls **`burnMembershipNFT(walletAddress)`** in `thirdweb-engine.ts`: - GETs owned tokens via `erc721/get-owned?ownerWallet=...` - If tokens exist, POSTs `erc721/burn` with the latest token ID 3. Logs success/failure --- ### Graceful Degradation The system has mock fallbacks at every layer: - **No ThirdWeb client ID** → `MockThirdWebAuth` with dummy wallet - **No Stripe keys** → `MockStripeCheckout` with simulated payment - **No ThirdWeb Engine config** → mint/burn skipped with console warnings - **No Sanity CMS** → hardcoded demo article from `constants.ts` ``` /demo └─ MembershipProvider + ThirdWebProvider └─ BlogPost (premium, clipped) ├─ PaywallOverlay │ ├─ Step 1: ThirdWebAuth → setWalletAddress │ └─ Step 2: StripeProvider → StripeCheckout → confirmPayment │ └─ Redirect /demo?success=true → isUnlocked │ ├─ Full article content (when unlocked) └─ SubscriptionManager (when unlocked) └─ Cancel → cancel_at_period_end: true Webhooks: invoice.payment_succeeded → mintMembershipNFT (ERC-721) customer.subscription.deleted → burnMembershipNFT (ERC-721) ```

Why did you wrap the Membership/ThirdWeb in providers?
Assistant17:03:56
That wasn't my decision — that's the existing architecture I worked within. `MembershipProvider` and `ThirdWebProviderWrapper` were already in `src/app/demo/DemoContent.tsx` before I made any changes. My changes were limited to: 1. Adding `burnMembershipNFT` to `thirdweb-engine.ts` 2. Creating the two new API routes (`cancel-subscription`, `subscription-status`) 3. Updating the webhook's `customer.subscription.deleted` handler 4. Creating `SubscriptionManager` and rendering it in `BlogPost` If your question is about the architectural reasoning behind the provider pattern itself — they use React Context so that any nested component (`PaywallOverlay`, `StripeCheckout`, `BlogPost`, etc.) can read/write shared state (`walletAddress`, `paymentStatus`, `isUnlocked`) without prop drilling. `ThirdWebProviderWrapper` specifically is required by the ThirdWeb SDK so its hooks (`useActiveAccount`, etc.) work in child components.
User (Turn 20)17:06:01
Got it- thanks. What does our smart contract look like? How is it structured?
Assistant17:06:11
There's no smart contract in this codebase. The project doesn't contain any Solidity files, Hardhat/Foundry config, or contract source code. The membership NFT system relies entirely on **ThirdWeb Engine as a managed service** — `thirdweb-engine.ts` makes HTTP calls to an external Engine instance that handles the on-chain operations: - **Mint**: `POST /contract/{chain}/{address}/erc721/mint-to` - **Burn**: `POST /contract/{chain}/{address}/erc721/burn` - **Read owned**: `GET /contract/{chain}/{address}/erc721/get-owned` The contract address and chain ID come from environment variables (`NFT_CONTRACT_ADDRESS`, `NFT_CHAIN_ID`), meaning the ERC-721 contract is deployed and managed outside this repo. We just talk to it through Engine's REST API using a backend wallet (`THIRDWEB_ENGINE_BACKEND_WALLET`). So to understand the contract's structure, you'd need to look at wherever it was deployed — likely through ThirdWeb's dashboard or a separate deployment repo. From this codebase's perspective, we just know it's a standard ERC-721 that supports mint-to and burn operations.

Input{ "file_path": "/Users/josephgenest/.claude/plans/linear-rolling-scott.md", "content": "# Soulbound Membership NFT Smart Contract\n\n## Context\nThe app uses ThirdWeb Engine to mint/burn ERC-721 membership NFTs, but there's no contract in the repo \u2014 it's assumed to be deployed externally. We need to write and include the actual Solidity contract so it can be version-controlled, tested, and deployed. The contract must be compatible with the ThirdWeb Engine API calls already in `src/app/lib/thirdweb-engine.ts`.\n\n**User choices**: Base network, soulbound (non-transferable), Foundry toolchain.\n\n## Contract Requirements (derived from `thirdweb-engine.ts`)\n\nThe Engine calls we already make dictate the contract interface:\n\n1. **`mintMembershipNFT`** calls `erc721/mint-to` with `{ receiver, metadata }` \u2192 contract needs a `mintTo(address, string)` function (ThirdWeb's standard ERC721 mint pattern)\n2. **`burnMembershipNFT`** calls `erc721/burn` with `{ tokenId }` \u2192 contract needs a `burn(uint256)` function callable by the backend wallet (not just the token owner)\n3. **`erc721/get-owned`** \u2192 standard `balanceOf`/`tokenOfOwnerByIndex` (ERC721Enumerable) or ThirdWeb's built-in owned-token indexing\n4. **Soulbound** \u2192 override `_update` to block transfers (allow only mint and burn)\n5. **Access control** \u2192 only the backend wallet (minter role) should mint and burn\n\n## File Changes\n\n### 1. CREATE `contracts/` Foundry project structure\n```\ncontracts/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 foundry.toml\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 src/\n\u2502 \u2514\u2500\u2500 PaywallTimesMembership.sol\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 test/\n\u2502 \u2514\u2500\u2500 PaywallTimesMembership.t.sol\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 script/\n \u2514\u2500\u2500 Deploy.s.sol\n```\n\n### 2. CREATE `contracts/foundry.toml`\nStandard Foundry config with OpenZeppelin remappings via soldeer or git submodules. Solidity 0.8.24+. Base chain config for deployment.\n\n### 3. CREATE `contracts/src/PaywallTimesMembership.sol`\nERC-721 contract inheriting from OpenZeppelin:\n- `ERC721`, `ERC721Enumerable`, `ERC721URIStorage`, `AccessControl`\n- `MINTER_ROLE` granted to the deployer (backend wallet)\n- `mintTo(address to, string memory uri)` \u2014 mints next token ID to `to`, sets token URI. Restricted to `MINTER_ROLE`.\n- `burn(uint256 tokenId)` \u2014 burns token. Restricted to `MINTER_ROLE` (not just owner, since the backend wallet burns on subscription end).\n- `_update()` override \u2014 reverts on transfers between non-zero addresses (soulbound). Only allows mint (from=0) and burn (to=0).\n- Auto-incrementing token ID counter.\n- Constructor sets name=\"The Paywall Times Membership\", symbol=\"TPTM\".\n\n### 4. CREATE `contracts/script/Deploy.s.sol`\nFoundry deployment script:\n- Deploys `PaywallTimesMembership`\n- Grants `MINTER_ROLE` to deployer (already default admin)\n- Logs deployed address\n\n## Implementation Order\n1. `foundry.toml` + install OpenZeppelin dependency\n2. `PaywallTimesMembership.sol`\n3. `PaywallTimesMembership.t.sol`\n4. `Deploy.s.sol`\n\n## No Changes to Existing Files\nThe contract is additive. `thirdweb-engine.ts` and the API routes remain unchanged \u2014 ThirdWeb Engine translates its REST API into the standard ERC-721 calls this contract exposes.\n\n## Verification\n1. `cd contracts && forge build` \u2014 compiles without errors\n2. `forge test -vvv` \u2014 all tests pass\n3. We need to write and include the actual Solidity contract so it can be version-controlled, tested, and deployed. The contract must be compatible with the ThirdWeb Engine API calls already in `src/app/lib/thirdweb-engine.ts`.\n\n**User choices**: Base network, soulbound (non-transferable), Foundry toolchain.\n\n## Contract Requirements (derived from `thirdweb-engine.ts`)\n\nThe Engine calls we already make dictate the contract interface:\n\n1. **`mintMembershipNFT`** calls `erc721/mint-to` with `{ receiver, metadata }` \u2192 contract needs a `mintTo(address, string)` function (ThirdWeb's standard ERC721 mint pattern)\n2. **`burnMembershipNFT`** calls `erc721/burn` with `{ tokenId }` \u2192 contract needs a `burn(uint256)` function callable by the backend wallet (not just the token owner)\n3. **`erc721/get-owned`** \u2192 standard `balanceOf`/`tokenOfOwnerByIndex` (ERC721Enumerable) or ThirdWeb's built-in owned-token indexing\n4. **Soulbound** \u2192 override `_update` to block transfers (allow only mint and burn)\n5. **Access control** \u2192 only the backend wallet (minter role) should mint and burn\n\n## File Changes\n\n### 1. CREATE `contracts/` Foundry project structure\n```\ncontracts/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 foundry.toml\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 src/\n\u2502 \u2514\u2500\u2500 PaywallTimesMembership.sol\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 test/\n\u2502 \u2514\u2500\u2500 PaywallTimesMembership.t.sol\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 script/\n \u2514\u2500\u2500 Deploy.s.sol\n```\n\n### 2. CREATE `contracts/foundry.toml`\nStandard Foundry config with OpenZeppelin remappings via soldeer or git submodules. Solidity 0.8.24+. Base chain config for deployment.\n\n### 3. CREATE `contracts/src/PaywallTimesMembership.sol`\nERC-721 contract inheriting from OpenZeppelin:\n- `ERC721`, `ERC721Enumerable`, `ERC721URIStorage`, `AccessControl`\n- `MINTER_ROLE` granted to the deployer (backend wallet)\n- `mintTo(address to, string memory uri)` \u2014 mints next token ID to `to`, sets token URI. Restricted to `MINTER_ROLE`.\n- `burn(uint256 tokenId)` \u2014 burns token. Restricted to `MINTER_ROLE` (not just owner, since the backend wallet burns on subscription end).\n- `_update()` override \u2014 reverts on transfers between non-zero addresses (soulbound). Only allows mint (from=0) and burn (to=0).\n- Auto-incrementing token ID counter.\n- Constructor sets name=\"The Paywall Times Membership\", symbol=\"TPTM\".\n\n### 4. CREATE `contracts/test/PaywallTimesMembership.t.sol`\nFoundry tests:\n- Minter can mint to an address\n- Non-minter cannot mint (reverts)\n- Minter can burn any token\n- Non-minter cannot burn (reverts)\n- Transfer between wallets reverts (soulbound)\n- `approve` and `setApprovalForAll` are blocked or irrelevant (transfer still reverts)\n- Token URI is stored and retrievable\n- Token IDs auto-increment\n\n### 5. CREATE `contracts/script/Deploy.s.sol`\nFoundry deployment script:\n- Deploys `PaywallTimesMembership`\n- Grants `MINTER_ROLE` to deployer (already default admin)\n- Logs deployed address\n\n## Implementation Order\n1. `foundry.toml` + install OpenZeppelin dependency\n2. `PaywallTimesMembership.sol`\n3. `PaywallTimesMembership.t.sol`\n4. `Deploy.s.sol`\n\n## No Changes to Existing Files\nThe contract is additive. `thirdweb-engine.ts` and the API routes remain unchanged \u2014 ThirdWeb Engine translates its REST API into the standard ERC-721 calls this contract exposes.\n\n## Verification\n1. `cd contracts && forge build` \u2014 compiles without errors\n2. `forge test -vvv` \u2014 all tests pass\n3. Manual: `forge script script/Deploy.s.sol --rpc-url base` with `--broadcast` to deploy (requires funded wallet + RPC URL)\n", "planFilePath": "/Users/josephgenest/.claude/plans/linear-rolling-scott.md" }
